3-Party Deal Making Platform — Software Design Document
Version: 1.0
Date: June 2026
Status: Draft for Review
Classification: Confidential

Executive Summary
The 3-Party Deal Making Platform is a domain-agnostic, cloud-native marketplace that
enables triadic value creation among three distinct party types: Suppliers (who hold
underutilized resources), Consumers (who desire specific outputs), and Enhancers (who
provide enabling expertise or services). The platform’s core value proposition is the “any
domain, any initiator, win-win-win” principle — any party type can initiate a deal in any
industry vertical, and every deal is mathematically validated to ensure all three parties
achieve positive net value.
Purpose
This document provides the comprehensive software design specification for the 3-Party Deal
Making Platform, integrating domain modeling, workflow architecture, system architecture,
API design, user experience design, and economic mechanisms into a single, cohesive
blueprint. It serves as the authoritative reference for engineering teams, product managers,
and stakeholders involved in building and evolving the platform.
The 3-Party Model at a Glance
The platform breaks away from traditional two-sided marketplaces by formalizing a threesided structure:
•
•
•

Supplier holds an underutilized resource or asset (e.g., idle farmland, vacant building,
unused vehicle, idle machinery) and seeks to derive value from it.
Consumer desires a specific output, product, or service (e.g., crop produce, rental
space, transportation, processed goods).
Enhancer bridges the gap by providing enabling input, expertise, or services (e.g.,
agrodealer furnishing seeds/fertilizer, contractor performing renovation, mechanic
providing maintenance).

Any party can initiate a deal. Each party may be an individual, organization, or a PartyGroup
— a collective of people/entities pooling resources or needs. The platform validates that
every deal satisfies the Win-Win-Win Principle: all three parties must receive net positive
value.

Feature
Multi-Party Matching

Description
Algorithmic matching of compatible Suppliers,

benefit (see Chapter 8)

proposal versioning and threaded term dimensions

reputation system

PartyGroup entity enabling cooperatives,
partnerships, and corporate alliances to participate as
a single Party
Three-tier resolution: direct negotiation, platform
mediation, binding arbitration

Architecture Approach
The platform follows a microservices architecture with 16 core and supporting services,
communicating via a combination of synchronous REST/gRPC APIs and asynchronous
event-driven patterns via Apache Kafka. The architecture embraces:
•
•
•
•
•

Domain-Driven Design (DDD) with clear aggregate boundaries and ubiquitous
language
Event sourcing for deal lifecycle ensuring full audit trail
CQRS for read/write separation with near-realtime projections
Saga patterns for distributed transaction coordination
API-first design with versioned REST APIs, gRPC inter-service communication,
GraphQL queries, and WebSocket real-time updates

Intended Outcomes
•
Enable cross-domain deal creation with minimal platform customization
•
Reduce deal negotiation friction through algorithmic matching and fairness validation
•
Build trust among parties via transparent reputation scoring and escrow protection
•
Scale to support millions of parties and hundreds of thousands of concurrent deals
•
Achieve platform sustainability through a dynamic, trust-adjusted fee model

1. Introduction
1.1 Purpose
This Software Design Document (SDD) specifies the complete architecture, design, and
implementation blueprint for the 3-Party Deal Making Platform. It consolidates six specialistauthored design documents into a single unified reference covering:
•

Domain Model — Entities, relationships, value flow, and aggregate boundaries

•
•
•
•
•

Workflow Design — Deal lifecycle state machine, initiation flows, negotiation,
matching, execution
System Architecture — Microservices decomposition, communication patterns, data
architecture, security
API Design — REST APIs, events, webhooks, GraphQL schema
User Experience Design — User flows, wireframes, dashboards, notification design
Value Distribution & Economic Mechanisms — Value models, trust system, pricing,
risk management

The intended audience includes software architects, backend/frontend engineers, DevOps
engineers, product managers, QA engineers, and technical stakeholders.
1.2 Scope
This document covers the full design of the platform’s core capabilities:
In Scope: - Party management (individuals, organizations, groups) - Deal lifecycle from
creation through completion - Algorithmic matching and discovery - Multi-round negotiation
with versioning - Win-Win-Win validation engine - Escrow-based payment and settlement Trust scoring and reputation system - Review and rating mechanisms - Dispute resolution (3tier system) - Multi-channel notification system - Category/taxonomy system for domain
adaptability - Full microservices architecture with deployment topology - Complete API
specification (REST, gRPC, GraphQL, Events, Webhooks) - User experience flows and
interface specifications - Economic model: value distribution, pricing, risk management
Out of Scope: - Specific frontend framework implementation details - Detailed infrastructure
cost estimates - Regulatory compliance certification processes - Physical hardware
procurement

2. System Overview
2.1 The 3-Party Model (Supplier-Consumer-Enhancer)
The platform operates on a triadic economic model where three distinct roles collaborate to
create value that would be difficult or impossible to achieve in bilateral transactions.

Key insight: Unlike traditional two-sided marketplaces where the platform merely connects
supply and demand, the 3-Party Deal Making Platform actively orchestrates a value-creation
triangle. The Enhancer role is the critical differentiator — without the Enhancer’s input,
many Supplier-Consumer pairings would be economically infeasible or operationally
impractical.
Examples across domains:

Any party can initiate: A Supplier with idle land can find a Consumer needing crops and an
Enhancer to bridge the gap. A Consumer needing rental space can find a Supplier with a
vacant building and an Enhancer to renovate it. An Enhancer with processing expertise can
proactively identify Supplier-Consumer pairs that would benefit from their service.
2.2 Deal Lifecycle at a Glance
The deal lifecycle is the central orchestration mechanism of the platform. It defines the states
a deal progresses through from initial idea to final settlement.
[DRAFT] --> [SUGGESTED] --> [PENDING_REVIEW] --> [NEGOTIATING] -->
[TERMS_LOCKED]
|
v
[COMPLETED] <-- [EXECUTING] <-- [COMMITTED] <------------------------------- [AGREED]
|
^
|
|
+--> [SETTLED] --> [CLOSED]
[DISPUTED]
|
Alternative paths:
v
- Any state --> [CANCELLED] (withdrawal/breach)
[RESOLVED]
- NEGOTIATING --> [AWAITING_PARTY] (clarification requested)
|
- NEGOTIATING --> [ON_HOLD] (suspension)
|
- SUGGESTED/PENDING_REVIEW --> [EXPIRED] (timeout)
|
v
[TERMINATED]

The full 13-state deal lifecycle is specified in Chapter 4 (Workflow & State Machine Design).
For a detailed state machine diagram with all transitions, timeouts, and validation gates, see
Section 4.1.

Multi-Party Deal Facilitation Platform
Domain-Driven Design (DDD)

3. Overview & Domain Narrative
The platform facilitates triadic deals among three distinct party types:

•
•
•

Supplier: Holds an underutilized resource or asset (e.g., idle farmland, vacant
building, unused vehicle, idle machinery) and seeks to derive value from it.
Consumer: Desires a specific output, product, or service (e.g., crop produce, rental
space, transportation, processed goods).
Enhancer: Bridges the gap by providing enabling input, expertise, or services (e.g.,
agrodealer furnishing seeds/fertilizer, contractor performing renovation, mechanic
providing maintenance).

Any party can initiate a deal. Each party may be an individual, organization, or a PartyGroup
(a collective of people/entities pooling resources or needs). The platform validates that every
deal satisfies the Win-Win-Win Principle: all three parties must receive net positive value.
The platform operates across any domain, using a flexible categorization system that allows
deals to be classified by industry, geography, resource type, and output type.

3.2 Detailed Value Flow by Party

Supplier Value Flow

INPUTS:
OUTPUTS:
├── Resource/Asset (land, building, ├── Reward Share (from ValueDistribution)
│ vehicle, machinery)
│ (can be: fixed fee, revenue share,
├── Availability (time, access)
│ in-kind benefit, hybrid)
├── Maintenance/upkeep responsibility ├── Enhanced asset value (resource may
└── Risk bearing (asset depreciation) │ be improved by enhancement)
├── Potential ongoing revenue stream
└── TrustScore increase on completion

Consumer Value Flow

INPUTS:
OUTPUTS:
├── Payment/Value (to platform escrow) ├── Desired Output (crop produce, rental
├── Clear requirement specification │ space, transportation, processed goods)
├── Timely payment
├── Quality-assured deliverable
└── Feedback/review
├── Convenience (single deal, 3-party
│ orchestration handled by platform)
└── Potential long-term supply relationship

Enhancer Value Flow

INPUTS:
OUTPUTS:
├── Expertise/Skills
├── Fee/Share (from ValueDistribution)
├── Materials/Inputs (seeds, fertilizer,│ (can be: fixed fee, hourly rate,
│ tools, equipment)
│ revenue share, milestone payments)
├── Labor/Time
├── Portfolio expansion (new domains,
├── Risk bearing (input quality)
│ new relationships)
└── Quality guarantee
├── TrustScore as Enhancer
└── Potential recurring engagement

Platform Value Flow

INPUTS:
OUTPUTS:
├── Facilitation technology
├── Commission/Fee (% of deal value)
├── Matching algorithm
├── Data insights (market trends,
├── Escrow/payment processing
│ pricing benchmarks)
├── Dispute resolution
├── Network effects (more parties,
├── Trust/reputation system
│ more deals)
└── Legal framework (terms, agreements) └── Platform sustainability

3.3 Value Distribution Mechanics
The ValueDistribution entity enforces the Win-Win-Win Principle through the following
calculation:
Total Deal Value = Consumer Payment
Distributions:
├── Supplier Share = totalValue × supplierSharePercent
├── Enhancer Share = totalValue × enhancerSharePercent
├── Platform Fee
= totalValue × platformFeePercent
└── Consumer Surplus = totalValue - (supplier + enhancer + platform)
(value received - value paid)
Validation Rules:
1. supplierSharePercent + enhancerSharePercent + platformFeePercent = 100%
2. Each party's net value must be > 0 (positive for all three)
3. Consumer surplus ≥ minimum acceptable threshold (platform-defined)
4. The winWinWinScore must be ≥ platform minimum (e.g., 60/100)

3.4 Payment Flow Sequence

1. CONSUMER deposits funds → Platform ESCROW
2. ENHANCER delivers enhancement → Milestone verified
└── Partial release: enhancerShare released from escrow
3. SUPPLIER provides resource access → Milestone verified
└── Partial release: supplierShare released from escrow
4. CONSUMER receives output → Confirms satisfaction
└── Final release: remaining shares distributed
5. PLATFORM FEE automatically deducted at each release
6. If DISPUTE → Funds frozen → Resolution → Reallocation

3.2 Win-Win-Win Validation Algorithm

def validate_win_win_win(deal, value_distribution):

"""
Validates that a deal is positive for all three parties.
Returns: (is_valid, score, reasons)
"""
scores = {}
reasons = []

# Supplier value check

supplier_value = value_distribution.supplier_share_amount
supplier_cost = deal.resource.opportunity_cost # estimated
supplier_net = supplier_value - supplier_cost
scores['supplier'] = max(0, min(100, (supplier_net / max(supplier_cost, 1)) * 100))
if supplier_net <= 0:
reasons.append("Supplier net value is non-positive")

# Consumer value check

consumer_payment = value_distribution.consumer_cost_amount
consumer_received_value = deal.need.estimated_fulfillment_value
consumer_net = consumer_received_value - consumer_payment
scores['consumer'] = max(0, min(100, (consumer_net / max(consumer_payment, 1)) *
100))
if consumer_net <= 0:
reasons.append("Consumer net value is non-positive")

# Enhancer value check

enhancer_value = value_distribution.enhancer_share_amount
enhancer_cost = deal.enhancement.estimated_input_cost
enhancer_net = enhancer_value - enhancer_cost
scores['enhancer'] = max(0, min(100, (enhancer_net / max(enhancer_cost, 1)) * 100))
if enhancer_net <= 0:
reasons.append("Enhancer net value is non-positive")

# Composite score (geometric mean ensures all must be positive)

import math
composite = math.pow(scores['supplier'] * scores['consumer'] * scores['enhancer'], 1/3)
is_valid = all(v > 0 for v in [supplier_net, consumer_net, enhancer_net])
is_valid = is_valid and composite >= PLATFORM_MIN_WIN_SCORE # e.g., 60
return is_valid, composite, reasons

3.2 Recommended Indexes
-- Party lookups

CREATE INDEX idx_party_email ON Party(email);
CREATE INDEX idx_party_location ON Party USING GIST(location);
CREATE INDEX idx_party_type ON Party(partyType, isActive);

-- Deal queries

CREATE INDEX idx_deal_status ON Deal(dealStatus, isPublic);
CREATE INDEX idx_deal_category ON Deal(domainCategoryId, dealStatus);
CREATE INDEX idx_deal_location ON Deal USING GIST(location);
CREATE INDEX idx_deal_initiator ON Deal(initiatorPartyId, createdAt DESC);

-- Participation

CREATE INDEX idx_participation_party ON DealParticipation(partyId,
participationStatus);
CREATE INDEX idx_participation_deal ON DealParticipation(dealId, role);

-- Match scoring

CREATE INDEX idx_match_party_supplier ON Match(supplierPartyId, matchStatus);
CREATE INDEX idx_match_party_consumer ON Match(consumerPartyId, matchStatus);
CREATE INDEX idx_match_party_enhancer ON Match(enhancerPartyId, matchStatus);
CREATE INDEX idx_match_score ON Match(matchScore DESC) WHERE matchStatus =
'PENDING';

-- Reviews

CREATE INDEX idx_review_reviewed ON Review(reviewedPartyId, createdAt DESC);
CREATE INDEX idx_review_deal ON Review(dealId, reviewerPartyId);

-- Messages

CREATE INDEX idx_message_sender ON Message(senderPartyId, createdAt DESC);
CREATE INDEX idx_message_recipient ON Message(recipientPartyId, isRead, createdAt
DESC);
CREATE INDEX idx_message_deal ON Message(dealId, createdAt DESC);

-- Transactions

CREATE INDEX idx_transaction_deal ON Transaction(dealId, createdAt DESC);
CREATE INDEX idx_transaction_party ON Transaction(fromPartyId, toPartyId, createdAt
DESC);

-- Categories

CREATE INDEX idx_category_parent ON Category(parentCategoryId, categoryType,
isActive);

-- Notifications

CREATE INDEX idx_notification_party ON Notification(partyId, isRead, createdAt DESC);

Term

Definition

Aggregate

A cluster of associated objects treated as a single unit for
data changes.
The single entity within an aggregate that serves as the
entry point and enforces invariants.
A business rule that must always be true, enforced within an
aggregate boundary.
A domain object with a unique identity that persists over
time.
An immutable object without identity, defined solely by its
attributes (e.g., GeoPoint, Money).
The core platform principle that all three parties must derive
positive net value.

4.3 Complete State Machine (Mermaid)
stateDiagram-v2
[*] --> DRAFT : Any party creates deal

DRAFT --> SUGGESTED : Initiator submits proposal
DRAFT --> CANCELLED : Initiator abandons
DRAFT --> EXPIRED : 7-day timeout
SUGGESTED --> PENDING_REVIEW : All parties invited
SUGGESTED --> CANCELLED : Counter-party rejects
SUGGESTED --> EXPIRED : 14-day timeout
PENDING_REVIEW --> NEGOTIATING : All parties acknowledge
PENDING_REVIEW --> CANCELLED : Initiator withdraws
PENDING_REVIEW --> EXPIRED : 14-day timeout
NEGOTIATING --> TERMS_LOCKED : All parties accept terms
NEGOTIATING --> AWAITING_PARTY : Party requests clarification/info
NEGOTIATING --> ON_HOLD : Party requests hold / Platform suspends
NEGOTIATING --> CANCELLED : Any party withdraws
NEGOTIATING --> EXPIRED : 30-day timeout
AWAITING_PARTY --> NEGOTIATING : Requested party responds
AWAITING_PARTY --> ON_HOLD : 14-day no-response
AWAITING_PARTY --> CANCELLED : Any party withdraws
TERMS_LOCKED --> COMMITTED : All parties sign commitment
TERMS_LOCKED --> NEGOTIATING : Any party requests renegotiation

TERMS_LOCKED --> CANCELLED : 14-day timeout / Any party withdraws
COMMITTED --> EXECUTING : Auto-transition after 3-day prep
COMMITTED --> CANCELLED : Unanimous withdrawal within 3 days
EXECUTING --> COMPLETED : All milestones verified
EXECUTING --> DISPUTED : Any party raises dispute
EXECUTING --> AWAITING_PARTY : Party delays milestone
EXECUTING --> ON_HOLD : Platform/Party suspends
EXECUTING --> CANCELLED : Mutual agreement / Breach termination
ON_HOLD --> NEGOTIATING : Hold reason resolved
ON_HOLD --> EXECUTING : Hold reason resolved
ON_HOLD --> CANCELLED : 30-day hold timeout
DISPUTED --> EXECUTING : Dispute resolved, resume
DISPUTED --> COMPLETED : Dispute resolved, partial completion
DISPUTED --> CANCELLED : Dispute resolved, terminate
DISPUTED --> ON_HOLD : Awaiting external arbitration
COMPLETED --> [*]
CANCELLED --> [*]
EXPIRED --> [*]

4.6 Win-Win Validation Gate
Every state transition toward commitment must pass the Win-Win-Win Validation Gate:
VALIDATION_CRITERIA:
├── Economic Value Check
│ ├── Each party's net benefit > 0 (after costs/fees)
│ ├── No party's cost exceeds 80% of their stated budget/capacity
│ └── Total deal value ≥ platform minimum threshold
├── Balance Check
│ ├── No single party captures > 70% of total surplus
│ ├── Gini coefficient of value distribution ≤ 0.5
│ └── Each party's ROI ≥ platform floor (5% minimum)
├── Feasibility Check
│ ├── Supplier resource available in required timeframe
│ ├── Consumer need matches supplier output (type, quantity, quality)
│ └── Enhancer capability matches required value-add
├── Risk Check
│ ├── No party has > 3 active deals in EXECUTING state
│ └── No previous CANCELLED/DISPUTED pattern (3-strike rule)
└── Compliance Check
├── All parties KYC/AML verified
├── Deal category not on restricted list
└── Regulatory requirements met for jurisdiction

4. Initiation Workflows
4.1 Supplier-Initiated Deal Flow
Scenario: Supplier (S) has idle arable farm. Finds Consumer (C) needing crop produce.
Identifies Enhancer (E) - agrodealer with seeds/fertilizer.
┌─────────┐ ┌─────────┐ ┌─────────┐ ┌─────────┐
┌─────────┐
│ STEP 1 │ ──→ │ STEP 2 │ ──→ │ STEP 3 │ ──→ │ STEP 4 │ ──→ │
STEP 5 │
│ Create │ │ Define │ │ Search │ │ Invite │ │ Platform│
│ Draft │ │ Terms │ │ C + E │ │ Parties │ │ Validate│
└─────────┘ └─────────┘ └─────────┘
└─────────┘ └─────────┘
│
│
│
│

4. Negotiation Workflow
4.1 Negotiation Architecture Overview
The negotiation phase (S3: NEGOTIATING) is the most complex interaction in the deal
lifecycle. It supports parallel multi-threaded negotiations on different term dimensions, with
the ability to lock individual dimensions before finalizing all terms.
Core Principles: 1. Threaded Negotiation: Each term dimension can be negotiated
independently 2. Version Control: Every proposal is versioned; full audit trail maintained 3.
Counter-Party Protection: No party can unilaterally change locked terms 4. Time-Bound: All
negotiations have explicit deadlines 5. Win-Win Enforcement: Platform validates no party is
disadvantaged
4.2 Negotiable Term Dimensions
┌────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────
───────────────────────┐
│ Dimension
│ Negotiable Elements
│
├────────────────────────┼───────────────
───────────────────────────────────────┤
│ VALUE_DISTRIBUTION │ Revenue/cost shares, percentages, absolute amounts
│
│
│ Payment schedule, escrow terms, penalty clauses
│
├────────────────────────┼───────────────
───────────────────────────────────────┤
│ DELIVERABLES
│ Output specifications, quality standards, quantities │
│
│ Acceptance criteria, inspection procedures
│
├────────────────────────┼───────────────
───────────────────────────────────────┤
│ TIMELINE
│ Start date, milestone dates, completion deadline │
│
│ Extension conditions, early completion bonuses
│
├────────────────────────┼───────────────
───────────────────────────────────────┤
│ ROLES_RESPONSIBILITIES │ Specific duties per party, reporting lines
│
│
│ Decision-making authority, sub-contracting rights │
├────────────────────────┼───────────────
───────────────────────────────────────┤
│ RISK_ALLOCATION
│ Liability limits, insurance requirements
│
│
│ Force majeure, indemnification, guarantee terms
│
├────────────────────────┼───────────────
───────────────────────────────────────┤
│ TERMINATION
│ Exit clauses, notice periods, termination for cause │
│
│ Asset return, IP ownership, post-termination duties │
└────────────────────────┴───────────────
───────────────────────────────────────┘

4.5 Value Distribution Negotiation Framework
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────────┐
│
VALUE DISTRIBUTION NEGOTIATION MODEL
│
├────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────────
┤
│
│
│ TOTAL DEAL VALUE = Consumer Revenue / Savings - Direct Costs - Platform Fees
│
│
│
│
┌────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────────────┐
│
│ │ DISTRIBUTION CONSTRAINTS
│
│
│ │ ├── Each party MIN: 5% of total value
│
│
│ │ ├── Each party MAX: 70% of total value
│
│
│ │ ├── Platform fee: 2-5% (auto-deducted, not negotiable)
│
│
│ │ └── Surplus distribution: Weighted by contribution + risk
│
│
│
└────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────────────┘
│
│
│
│ NEGOTIATION MECHANICS:
│
│ ┌─────────────┐ ┌─────────────┐
┌─────────────┐ ┌─────────────┐ │
│ │ Anchoring │───→│ Concession │───→│ ZOPA
│───→│
Agreement │ │
│ │ (opening) │ │ trading │ │ discovery │ │ point
│ │
│ └─────────────┘ └─────────────┘
└─────────────┘ └─────────────┘ │
│
│
│
┌────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────────────┐
│
│ │ PLATFORM NUDGES (shown to parties):
│
│
│ │ ├── "Market rate for similar deal: S=40%, C=35%, E=25%"
│
│
│ │ ├── "Your proposal: S=50%, C=30%, E=20% ← E is below market"
│
│
│ │ ├── "Surplus distribution Gini: 0.45 (fair)"
│
│
│ │ └── "Platform recommends: S=42%, C=33%, E=25%"
│
│
│
└────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────────────┘
│
│
│
└────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────────
┘

4.6 Parallel vs Sequential Negotiation Paths
Sequential Path (Default for simple deals):
Party A proposes → Party B responds → Party C responds → Revise → ... → Agreement

•
•

Used when: Deal value < $10K, 2-3 dimensions, parties prefer simplicity
Timeout: 72h per round, max 5 rounds

Parallel Path (Default for complex deals):
┌─→ Value Distribution Thread ─┐
│ (Party A ↔ Party B ↔ C) │
│
├──→ Merge → Final Agreement
┌─────────────┐ ├─→ Deliverables Thread ─────┤
│ All parties │────→│ (Party A ↔ Party B ↔ C) │
│ enter
│ ├─→ Timeline Thread ─────────┤
│ negotiation │ │ (Party A ↔ Party B ↔ C) │
└─────────────┘ └─→ Risk Thread ─────────────┘
(Party A ↔ Party B ↔ C)

•
•
•

Used when: Deal value ≥ $10K, 4+ dimensions, multiple entities per party
Timeout: 72h per thread per round, max 5 rounds per thread
Merge: When all threads LOCKED or when initiator calls for merge

Hybrid Path (Adaptive):
Start Sequential ──→ If round count > 3 on any dimension ──→ Switch to Parallel
OR party count per role > 1

When any party consists of multiple entities (e.g., a Consumer group with 3 co-investors):
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

│ Any single authorized member can approve
│
│
│ (suitable for sole proprietorships)

─────────────────────────┤
│ MAJORITY
│ >50% of members must approve
│

│ (suitable for partnerships, small groups)

─────────────────────────┤
│ ALL
│ 100% of members must approve
│
│
│ (suitable for joint ventures, critical deals) │
├───────────────┼────────────────────────
─────────────────────────┤
│ THRESHOLD │ Custom threshold (e.g., 2 of 3, 75%)
│

│
│ (configurable per party per deal)
│
├───────────────┼────────────────────────
─────────────────────────┤
│ WEIGHTED
│ Approval weighted by ownership/equity share │
│
│ (suitable for companies with shareholders)

─────────────────────────┘

4. Matching & Discovery Workflow
4.1 Discovery Architecture
The platform employs a multi-channel discovery system combining algorithmic matching,
network exploration, and proactive opportunity identification.
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────┐

│
DISCOVERY CHANNELS
│
├─────────────────────┬──────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┤
│ Channel
│ Description
│
├─────────────────────┼──────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┤
│ Algorithmic Match │ Compatibility scoring based on profile data
│
│ Network Discovery │ 2nd/3rd degree connections, deal history
│
│ Opportunity Feed │ Proactive suggestions based on intent signals
│
│ Browse & Search │ Self-directed exploration of marketplace
│
│ Enhancer Brokerage │ Enhancer-initiated matchmaking (Section 2.3)
│
│ Deal Cloning
│ Template-based deal replication in new contexts
│
└─────────────────────┴──────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┘

4.2 Compatibility Scoring Algorithm
Overall Compatibility Score (0-100):
COMPATIBILITY_SCORE = w₁·Resource_Need_Match + w₂·Value_Alignment +
w₃·Trust_Score + w₄·Geographic_Fit + w₅·Temporal_Alignment + w₆·Historical_Success +
w₇·Risk_Profile_Match
Where: w₁=0.25, w₂=0.20, w₃=0.15, w₄=0.10, w₅=0.10, w₆=0.10, w₇=0.10
─────────────────────────────────────────
──────────────────────────────────────
Dimension 1: RESOURCE-NEED MATCH (w₁ = 0.25)
├── Type compatibility: Exact=1.0, Related=0.7, Convertible=0.4, Mismatch=0
├── Quantity match: |supply - demand| / max(supply, demand) → score = 1 - ratio
├── Quality alignment: Meets spec=1.0, Close=0.8, Requires upgrade=0.5
└── Capacity utilization: Optimal zone (60-90%) = 1.0, else degrades
Dimension 2: VALUE ALIGNMENT (w₂ = 0.20)
├── Price overlap: ZOPA exists=1.0, Nearby=0.7, No overlap=0
├── Value distribution compatibility: Gini < 0.3 = 1.0, < 0.5 = 0.7, > 0.5 = 0.3
└── Payment terms alignment: Matching=1.0, Flexible=0.8, Conflicting=0.3
Dimension 3: TRUST SCORE (w₃ = 0.15)
├── Platform tenure: Normalized years on platform (0-1)
├── Completion rate: Deals completed / Deals started
├── Rating average: 5-star scale normalized
├── Verification level: Basic=0.5, Verified=0.8, Premium=1.0
└── Dispute history: 1 - (disputes / total deals), floor at 0.3
Dimension 4: GEOGRAPHIC FIT (w₄ = 0.10)
├── Distance: < 10km=1.0, < 50km=0.9, < 200km=0.7, < 1000km=0.5, > 1000km=0.3
├── Logistics feasibility: Road/rail/sea/air connectivity score
└── Regulatory compatibility: Same jurisdiction=1.0, Compatible=0.7, Complex=0.3
Dimension 5: TEMPORAL ALIGNMENT (w₅ = 0.10)
├── Availability overlap: Jaccard index of available windows

├── Urgency match: Both urgent=1.0, One urgent=0.6, Neither urgent=0.8
└── Seasonal fit: In-season=1.0, Off-season=0.5, Wrong season=0.1
Dimension 6: HISTORICAL SUCCESS (w₆ = 0.10)
├── Prior deals together: Each successful deal +0.2 (max 1.0)
├── Similar deal success: Completed similar deal type=0.8
└── Mutual connections: Shared successful partners=+0.1 each
Dimension 7: RISK PROFILE MATCH (w₇ = 0.10)
├── Deal size comfort: Within party's typical range=1.0, Stretch=0.6
├── Risk tolerance: Matching profiles=1.0, Complementary=0.7, Clashing=0.3
└── Financial health: All parties solvent=1.0, Flagged=0.5

4.4 Matching Process Flow
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────┐
│
MATCHING PROCESS FLOW
│
├────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┤
│
│
│ STEP 1: PROFILE INGESTION
│
│ ├── Parse party profile (resource/need/capability)
│
│ ├── Extract structured attributes
│
│ ├── Geocode locations
│
│ └── Normalize units and currencies
│
│
│
│ STEP 2: ELIGIBILITY FILTERING
│
│ ├── Hard constraints check:
│
│ │ ├── Jurisdiction compatibility
│
│ │ ├── Regulatory compliance (e.g., export controls)
│
│ │ ├── Sanctions/PEP screening
│
│ │ ├── Minimum platform score threshold
│
│ │ └── Currently available (not at max deals)
│
│ └── Eliminate incompatible candidates
│
│
│
│ STEP 3: COMPATIBILITY SCORING
│
│ ├── Calculate 7-dimension score for each candidate pair/triplet
│
│ ├── Weight by recency (more recent profiles = higher weight)
│
│ └── Generate ranked candidate list
│
│
│
│ STEP 4: TRIAD ASSEMBLY
│
│ ├── For each Supplier-Consumer pair, find best Enhancer
│
│ ├── Validate triad feasibility (all three must be compatible)
│
│ ├── Score triad overall (weighted average of pairwise scores)
│
│ └── Ensure no party appears in conflicting triads
│
│
│
│ STEP 5: RANKING & DIVERSIFICATION
│
│ ├── Rank triads by overall score
│
│ ├── Apply diversity: max 3 triads with same Supplier
│
│ ├── Apply freshness: boost new listings
│
│ └── Generate final recommendation list
│
│
│
│ STEP 6: PRESENTATION
│
│ ├── Display top 10 triads to initiator
│
│ ├── For each: compatibility breakdown, estimated value, timeline
│
│ └── Enable filtering, sorting, and saved search
│
│
│
└────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┘

4.5 Deal Suggestion Engine
The platform proactively suggests deals based on:
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────┐

│
SUGGESTION TRIGGERS
│
├────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┤
│
│
│ TRIGGER 1: New resource/need posted
│
│ ├── Immediate match against existing pool
│
│ ├── Notify matched parties within 1 hour
│
│ └── Confidence threshold: 70+ for immediate, 50+ for digest
│
│
│
│ TRIGGER 2: Market opportunity detected
│
│ ├── Price/volume anomaly in market data
│
│ ├── Match underutilized resources with unmet needs
│
│ └── Notify relevant parties in daily opportunity digest
│
│
│
│ TRIGGER 3: Historical pattern match
│
│ ├── "Deals like this usually pair with..."
│
│ ├── Seasonal patterns (e.g., harvest timing)
│
│ └── Proactive suggestion 30 days before optimal window
│
│
│
│ TRIGGER 4: Network effect
│
│ ├── "Your partner X worked successfully with Y"
│
│ ├── Transitive trust: A↔B + B↔C → suggest A↔C
│
│ └── Weighted by mutual connection strength
│
│
│
│ TRIGGER 5: Enhancer alert
│
│ ├── Enhancer signals availability
│
│ ├── Platform finds best S-C pair for E
│
│ └── Triple-notification to all three parties
│
│
│
└────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┘

4.2 Milestone Tracking System
Milestone Structure:
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────┐
│
MILESTONE DEFINITION TEMPLATE
│
├──────────────────┬─────────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┤
│ Field
│ Description
│
├──────────────────┼─────────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┤
│ milestone_id │ Unique identifier (e.g., MS-001)
│
│ title
│ Short name (e.g., "Site Preparation")
│
│ description
│ Detailed deliverable description
│
│ owner
│ Party responsible for delivery
│
│ verifier
│ Party responsible for verification
│
│ due_date
│ Target completion date
│
│ predecessors │ Milestones that must complete first
│
│ deliverables │ Required evidence (photos, docs, signatures)
│
│ payment_trigger │ Amount released on completion
│
│ completion_criteria │ Measurable acceptance criteria
│
│ auto_verify
│ Can platform auto-verify? (Y/N)
│
│ dispute_window │ Hours allowed for challenge post-submission
│
└──────────────────┴─────────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┘

Milestone Status Flow:
stateDiagram-v2
[*] --> NOT_STARTED : Deal enters EXECUTING
NOT_STARTED --> IN_PROGRESS : Owner begins work
NOT_STARTED --> BLOCKED : Predecessor not complete
BLOCKED --> IN_PROGRESS : Predecessors complete
IN_PROGRESS --> SUBMITTED : Owner submits deliverables

IN_PROGRESS --> AT_RISK : < 24h to deadline, < 80% complete
IN_PROGRESS --> DELAYED : Past deadline
AT_RISK --> SUBMITTED : Owner submits
AT_RISK --> DELAYED : Deadline passes
DELAYED --> SUBMITTED : Owner submits late
DELAYED --> DISPUTED : Verifier challenges delay
SUBMITTED --> UNDER_REVIEW : Verifier begins review
SUBMITTED --> DISPUTED : Verifier challenges
UNDER_REVIEW --> ACCEPTED : Verifier approves (auto after 48h)
UNDER_REVIEW --> REJECTED : Verifier rejects with reason
UNDER_REVIEW --> DISPUTED : Verifier raises dispute
REJECTED --> IN_PROGRESS : Owner revises
REJECTED --> DISPUTED : Owner disputes rejection
ACCEPTED --> COMPLETED : Payment released
COMPLETED --> [*]
DISPUTED --> IN_PROGRESS : Resolved - continue
DISPUTED --> COMPLETED : Resolved - partial accept
DISPUTED --> CANCELLED : Resolved - terminate

4.3 Payment / Value Transfer Flow
The platform supports multiple payment models:
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────┐
│
PAYMENT MODEL OPTIONS
│
├─────────────────────┬──────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┤
│ Model
│ Mechanics
│
├─────────────────────┼──────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┤
│ ESCROW (Default) │ Platform holds funds; releases on milestone
│
│
│ verification. 3-party approval for release.
│
│
│ Best for: High-value, complex deals
│
├─────────────────────┼──────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┤
│ STAGED_DIRECT
│ Consumer pays directly at milestones; platform
│
│
│ tracks but doesn't hold funds. Auto-invoicing.
│
│
│ Best for: Trusted repeat partners
│
├─────────────────────┼──────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┤
│ PERFORMANCE_BOND │ Enhancer posts bond; forfeits on non-delivery.
│
│
│ Supplier and Consumer payments held in escrow.
│
│
│ Best for: Enhancer-dependent deals
│
├─────────────────────┼──────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┤
│ REVENUE_SHARE
│ Minimal upfront; automatic revenue splitting.
│
│
│ Smart-contract style distribution.
│
│
│ Best for: Joint ventures, ongoing operations
│
├─────────────────────┼──────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┤
│ HYBRID
│ Combination: Escrow for key milestones + direct
│
│
│ for minor milestones + revenue share for surplus. │
│
│ Best for: Large, multi-phase deals
│
└─────────────────────┴──────────────────
─────────────────────────────────────┘

│───→│ DEAL │
│ COMMITS │ │ FUNDING │ │ COMPLETE │ │ RELEASE │ │

┌────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────────────────┐
│ ESCROW RULES
│
│ ├── Funding must occur within 72h of COMMITTED state
│
│ ├── Partial funding → AWAITING_PARTY until fully funded
│
│ ├── Unfunded after 7 days → CANCELLED
│
│ ├── Release requires: milestone ACCEPTED + 24h dispute window clear │
│ ├── Dispute freezes all releases until resolved
│
│ ├── Platform fee (2-5%) deducted at each release
│
│ └── Refund on CANCELLED: pro-rata minus platform fees
│
└────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────────────────────┘

4.1 Overall Deal Lifecycle Swimlane

%%{init: {'theme': 'base', 'themeVariables': { 'primaryColor': '#e1f5fe', 'primaryTextColor':

sequenceDiagram
actor Initiator as Initiator
actor Counter1 as Counter-Party 1
actor Counter2 as Counter-Party 2
participant Platform as Platform Engine
participant Escrow as Escrow Service
Note over Initiator, Escrow: PHASE 1: INITIATION
Initiator->>Platform: Create Deal Draft
Platform-->>Initiator: Confirm DRAFT state
Initiator->>Platform: Submit Proposal
Platform->>Counter1: Send Invitation
Platform->>Counter2: Send Invitation
Platform-->>Initiator: SUGGESTED state
Note over Initiator, Escrow: PHASE 2: REVIEW & ACK
Counter1->>Platform: Acknowledge Proposal
Counter2->>Platform: Acknowledge Proposal
Platform-->>Initiator,Counter1,Counter2: NEGOTIATING state
Note over Initiator, Escrow: PHASE 3: NEGOTIATION
par Term Thread 1: Value Distribution
Initiator->>Platform: Propose 40/35/25 split
Platform->>Counter1: Notify proposal
Platform->>Counter2: Notify proposal
Counter1->>Platform: Counter: 42/33/25
Counter2->>Platform: Accept
Initiator->>Platform: Accept counter
Platform-->>Initiator,Counter1,Counter2: Value dim LOCKED
and Term Thread 2: Timeline
Counter1->>Platform: Propose 90-day timeline
Initiator->>Platform: Counter: 60 days
Counter2->>Platform: Accept 60 days
Counter1->>Platform: Accept 60 days
Platform-->>Initiator,Counter1,Counter2: Timeline dim LOCKED
end
Note over Initiator, Escrow: PHASE 4: COMMITMENT
Platform->>Initiator,Counter1,Counter2: All terms LOCKED
Initiator->>Platform: Sign Commitment
Counter1->>Platform: Sign Commitment

Counter2->>Platform: Sign Commitment
Platform->>Escrow: Initialize Escrow Account
Escrow-->>Platform: Account Ready
Platform-->>Initiator,Counter1,Counter2: COMMITTED state
Note over Initiator, Escrow: PHASE 5: EXECUTION
Counter1->>Escrow: Fund Escrow (100%)
Escrow-->>Platform: Confirm Funding
Platform-->>Initiator,Counter1,Counter2: EXECUTING state
loop Per Milestone
Initiator->>Platform: Submit Milestone Evidence
Platform->>Counter1: Request Verification
Counter1->>Platform: Verify & Accept
Platform->>Escrow: Release Milestone Payment
Escrow-->>Counter2: Transfer Payment
Platform-->>Initiator,Counter1,Counter2: Milestone Complete
end
Note over Initiator, Escrow: PHASE 6: COMPLETION
Platform->>Initiator,Counter1,Counter2: All Milestones Complete
Platform->>Escrow: Release Final Payment
Escrow-->>Initiator: Final Transfer
Platform->>Initiator,Counter1,Counter2: Request Ratings
Initiator->>Platform: Submit Ratings
Counter1->>Platform: Submit Ratings
Counter2->>Platform: Submit Ratings
Platform-->>Initiator,Counter1,Counter2: COMPLETED state

4.2 Supplier-Initiated Deal Flow Swimlane
sequenceDiagram
actor S as Supplier
actor C as Consumer
actor E as Enhancer
participant Platform as Platform
participant Matcher as Matching Engine
participant Escrow as Escrow Service

Note over S,Escrow: SUPPLIER INITIATION FLOW
S->>Platform: Login → "Create Deal"
Platform-->>S: Display Resource Template
S->>Platform: Describe Resource (idle farm, 50 acres)
S->>Platform: Set Availability & Output Specs
S->>Platform: Set Value Share Expectation (40%)
S->>Platform: "Find Matches"
Platform->>Matcher: Query: Suppliers with farm → Consumers needing crops
Matcher->>Platform: Return ranked Consumer list
Platform-->>S: Display Consumer matches with scores
S->>Platform: Select Consumer C (score: 92)

Platform->>Matcher: Query: Enhancers for farm+crop deals
Matcher->>Platform: Return ranked Enhancer list
Platform-->>S: Display Enhancer matches
S->>Platform: Select Enhancer E (score: 88)
S->>Platform: Propose Value Split: S=40%, C=35%, E=25%
S->>Platform: Propose Milestones (8 steps)
S->>Platform: Submit Deal Proposal
Platform->>Platform: Run Win-Win-Win Validation
Platform-->>S: Validation Passed → SUGGESTED
Platform->>C: Send Deal Invitation (email + in-app)
Platform->>E: Send Deal Invitation (email + in-app)
alt Consumer Accepts
C->>Platform: Acknowledge & Review
Platform-->>C: Display Full Proposal
C->>Platform: Accept Negotiation
else Consumer Declines
C->>Platform: Decline with Reason
Platform-->>S: Notification: C declined, suggest alternatives
S->>Platform: Select Alternative Consumer
end
alt Enhancer Accepts
E->>Platform: Acknowledge & Review
Platform-->>E: Display Full Proposal
E->>Platform: Accept Negotiation
else Enhancer Declines
E->>Platform: Decline with Reason
Platform-->>S: Notification: E declined, suggest alternatives
S->>Platform: Select Alternative Enhancer
end
Platform-->>S,C,E: All parties accepted → NEGOTIATING
Note over S,Escrow: NEGOTIATION
C->>Platform: Counter: Value Split S=38%, C=37%, E=25%
E->>Platform: Accept C's counter
S->>Platform: Accept C's counter
Platform-->>S,C,E: TERMS_LOCKED
S->>Platform: Sign Commitment
C->>Platform: Sign Commitment
E->>Platform: Sign Commitment
Platform->>Escrow: Initialize Escrow
Platform-->>S,C,E: COMMITTED → EXECUTING in 3 days
Note over S,Escrow: EXECUTION
C->>Escrow: Fund Escrow ($100K)
Platform-->>S,C,E: EXECUTING

S->>Platform: Submit Milestone 1: Land Prep (photos)
E->>Platform: Verify: Accept
Platform->>Escrow: Release $10K → S
E->>Platform: Submit Milestone 2: Seeds Delivered (invoice)
S->>Platform: Verify: Accept
Platform->>Escrow: Release $15K → E
Note over S,Escrow: ... (milestones 3-8) ...
S->>Platform: Submit Milestone 8: Final Delivery
E->>Platform: Verify: Accept
C->>Platform: Verify Quality: Accept
Platform->>Escrow: Release Final $10K → S
Platform-->>S,C,E: COMPLETED
S->>Platform: Rate C (5★) and E (5★)
C->>Platform: Rate S (5★) and E (4★)
E->>Platform: Rate S (5★) and C (5★)
Platform-->>S,C,E: Deal Closed, Reputation Updated

4.3 Negotiation Flow Swimlane

sequenceDiagram
actor P1 as Party A
actor P2 as Party B
actor P3 as Party C
participant Platform as Platform
participant Mediator as Deal Coordinator
Note over P1,Mediator: NEGOTIATION PHASE ENTRY
Platform->>P1,P2,P3: All parties in NEGOTIATING state
Platform->>P1,P2,P3: Display Negotiation Dashboard
Note over P1,Mediator: PARALLEL THREAD 1: VALUE DISTRIBUTION
P1->>Platform: Propose: P1=45%, P2=35%, P3=20%
Platform->>P2: Notify: P1 proposes value split
Platform->>P3: Notify: P1 proposes value split
Platform-->>P1,P2,P3: Show: Gini=0.47, E is below market
P2->>Platform: Counter: P1=42%, P2=35%, P3=23%
P3->>Platform: Request Info: "Can P1 reduce to 40%?"
Platform-->>P1: P3 requests info on your position
P1->>Platform: Respond: "42% is my floor"
Platform-->>P3: P1 responds: 42% is floor
P3->>Platform: Accept P2's counter (42/35/23)
P1->>Platform: Accept P2's counter
Platform-->>P1,P2,P3: VALUE DISTRIBUTION LOCKED (42/35/23)
Note over P1,Mediator: PARALLEL THREAD 2: TIMELINE
P3->>Platform: Propose: 120-day timeline

P1->>Platform: Counter: 90-day timeline
P2->>Platform: Counter: 100-day timeline
P1->>Platform: Accept 100 days
P3->>Platform: Accept 100 days
Platform-->>P1,P2,P3: TIMELINE LOCKED (100 days)
Note over P1,Mediator: MERGE & LOCK
Platform->>Platform: Check: All dimensions LOCKED?
Platform->>Platform: Run Win-Win-Win Validation
Platform-->>P1,P2,P3: VALIDATION PASSED
Note over P1,Mediator: TERMS LOCKED → COMMITMENT
Platform->>P1,P2,P3: Present Final Term Sheet
P1->>Platform: Review & Approve
P2->>Platform: Review & Approve
P3->>Platform: Review & Approve
alt Internal Approval Needed (P2 has 3 members)
P2->>Platform: Initiate Internal Vote
Platform-->>P2: Distribute to P2-M1, P2-M2, P2-M3
P2-M1->>Platform: Approve
P2-M2->>Platform: Approve
P2-M3->>Platform: Reject (wants 38% for P2)
Platform-->>P2: 2/3 majority → Approved (MAJORITY rule)
end
P1->>Platform: Digital Signature
P2->>Platform: Digital Signature
P3->>Platform: Digital Signature
Platform-->>P1,P2,P3: TERMS_LOCKED → COMMITTED

4.4 Dispute Resolution Flow Swimlane

sequenceDiagram
actor P1 as Disputing Party
actor P2 as Accused Party
actor P3 as Third Party
participant Platform as Platform
participant Mediator as Mediator
participant Arb as Arbitration (optional)
Note over P1,Arb: DISPUTE RAISED
P1->>Platform: Raise Dispute (Category: QUALITY_SHORTFALL)
P1->>Platform: Upload Evidence (photos, docs)
P1->>Platform: Pay Dispute Deposit (2%)
Platform->>Platform: Validate Dispute
Platform-->>P1: Dispute Valid → Case #D-1042 Created
Platform->>P2: Notify: Dispute Raised by P1
Platform->>P3: Notify: Dispute Raised (informational)
Platform->>Escrow: FREEZE all pending payments

P2->>Platform: Submit Defense + Counter-Evidence
Platform-->>P1: P2 has submitted defense (evidence summary)
Note over P1,Arb: MEDIATION
Platform->>Mediator: Assign Case #D-1042
Mediator->>Platform: Review Case File
Mediator->>P1: Request Clarification
P1->>Mediator: Respond
Mediator->>P2: Request Clarification
P2->>Mediator: Respond
Mediator->>P1,P2,P3: Schedule Mediation Session
P1->>Mediator: Join Session
P2->>Mediator: Join Session
P3->>Mediator: Join Session (optional)
Note over P1,Arb: within session
Mediator->>P1,P2: Facilitate Discussion
Mediator->>P1,P2: Propose Resolution: Partial refund + revised milestone
alt Resolution Accepted
P1->>Platform: Accept Resolution
P2->>Platform: Accept Resolution
P3->>Platform: Accept Resolution
Platform->>Platform: Implement: Adjust escrow, update milestone
Platform-->>P1: Refund dispute deposit
Platform-->>P1,P2,P3: DISPUTE RESOLVED → Resume EXECUTING
else Resolution Rejected
P1->>Platform: Reject Resolution
Platform-->>P1,P2,P3: Offer: Re-mediation or Arbitration
alt Choose Arbitration
P1->>Platform: Request Arbitration
P2->>Platform: Agree to Arbitration
Platform->>Arb: Submit Case
Arb->>Arb: Review Evidence
Arb->>P1,P2: Binding Ruling
Platform->>Platform: Implement Ruling
Platform-->>P1,P2,P3: DISPUTE RESOLVED
else Choose Re-mediation
P1->>Platform: Request Re-mediation
Note over P1,Arb: Loop to mediation with new mediator
end
end
Note over P1,Arb: POST-RESOLUTION
P1->>Platform: Rate Resolution Process
P2->>Platform: Rate Resolution Process
Platform->>Platform: Update reputation scores
Platform->>Platform: Close Case #D-1042
Platform-->>P1,P2,P3: Final Resolution Summary

Appendix A: State Machine Formal Definition

STATES = { DRAFT, SUGGESTED, PENDING_REVIEW, NEGOTIATING,
AWAITING_PARTY,
TERMS_LOCKED, COMMITTED, EXECUTING, ON_HOLD, COMPLETED,
DISPUTED, CANCELLED, EXPIRED }
INITIAL_STATE = DRAFT
TERMINAL_STATES = { COMPLETED, CANCELLED, EXPIRED }
TRANSITIONS = {
(DRAFT, submit, SUGGESTED)
: [Initiator],
(DRAFT, abandon, CANCELLED)
: [Initiator],
(DRAFT, timeout, EXPIRED)
: [System],
(SUGGESTED, all_invited, PENDING_REVIEW) : [System],
(SUGGESTED, reject, CANCELLED)
: [CounterParty],
(SUGGESTED, timeout, EXPIRED)
: [System],
(PENDING_REVIEW, acknowledge, NEGOTIATING) : [AllParties],
(PENDING_REVIEW, withdraw, CANCELLED)
: [Initiator],
(PENDING_REVIEW, timeout, EXPIRED)
: [System],
(NEGOTIATING, lock_terms, TERMS_LOCKED) : [AllParties],
(NEGOTIATING, pause, AWAITING_PARTY)
: [AnyParty, System],
(NEGOTIATING, hold, ON_HOLD)
: [AnyParty, System],
(NEGOTIATING, withdraw, CANCELLED)
: [AnyParty],
(NEGOTIATING, timeout, ON_HOLD)
: [System],
(AWAITING_PARTY, respond, NEGOTIATING) : [TargetParty],
(AWAITING_PARTY, hold, ON_HOLD)
: [System],
(AWAITING_PARTY, withdraw, CANCELLED)
: [AnyParty],
(AWAITING_PARTY, timeout, ON_HOLD)
: [System],
(TERMS_LOCKED, commit, COMMITTED)
: [AllParties],
(TERMS_LOCKED, renegotiate, NEGOTIATING) : [AnyParty],
(TERMS_LOCKED, withdraw, CANCELLED)
: [AnyParty],
(TERMS_LOCKED, timeout, CANCELLED)
: [System],
(COMMITTED, begin, EXECUTING)
(COMMITTED, withdraw, CANCELLED)

: [System],
: [Unanimous],

(EXECUTING, complete, COMPLETED)
: [AllParties, System],
(EXECUTING, dispute, DISPUTED)
: [AnyParty],
(EXECUTING, pause, AWAITING_PARTY)
: [AnyParty],
(EXECUTING, hold, ON_HOLD)
: [AnyParty, System],
(EXECUTING, terminate, CANCELLED)
: [Mutual, System],
(ON_HOLD, resume_negotiating, NEGOTIATING) : [AnyParty],
(ON_HOLD, resume_executing, EXECUTING) : [AnyParty],

(ON_HOLD, cancel, CANCELLED)

}

: [System, AnyParty],

Appendix D: Glossary
Term
3-Party Deal
Commitment
Escrow
Milestone
Win-Win-Win
ZOPA
Gini Coefficient
Compatibility Score
Good-Faith Deposit
Enhancer

Definition
A transaction involving Supplier, Consumer, and Enhancer
roles
Binding agreement signed by all parties, triggering
execution
Third-party holding of funds until conditions are met
A defined checkpoint in execution with associated
deliverables and payments
The principle that all three parties must benefit from the
deal
Zone of Possible Agreement - the overlap between party
acceptable ranges
Measure of inequality in value distribution (0 = equal, 1 =
unequal)
Algorithmic measure of fit between parties (0-100)
Payment required to raise a dispute, discouraging frivolous
claims
Party that adds value to enable the Supplier-Consumer
transaction

Document Version: 1.0 | Status: Draft | For Review
Version: 1.0
Status: Production-Ready Architecture Blueprint
Classification: Internal - Confidential

5. Executive Summary
This document presents the comprehensive system architecture for a 3-Party Deal Making
Platform - a domain-agnostic, scalable marketplace that connects Suppliers, Consumers, and
Enhancers to create mutually beneficial deals. The architecture follows cloud-native
principles, microservices patterns, and event-driven design to support complex multi-party
negotiations across any industry domain.
Key Architectural Principles
Principle
Domain-Agnostic Design
Event-Driven Core

Description
Core services are generic; domain-specific logic
is pluggable via configuration and extensions
All state changes flow through events, enabling
loose coupling and extensibility

Principle
Data Sovereignty
** eventual Consistency**
Auditability by Design
API-First

Description
Each service owns its data; no direct database
access between services
Accepted for cross-service operations; strong
consistency within service boundaries
Complete event sourcing for deal lifecycle
ensures full audit trail
All services expose versioned APIs; consumerdriven contract testing

5.2 Deal Lifecycle States

[DRAFT] --> [PUBLISHED] --> [MATCHING] --> [NEGOTIATING] --> [VALIDATED]
|
v
[SIGNED] <-- [AGREED] <-- [ACCEPTED] <---------------------- [APPROVED]

|
v
[EXECUTING] --> [MILESTONE_REACHED] --> [COMPLETED]
|
v
[SETTLED] --> [CLOSED]
Alternative paths:
- Any state --> [CANCELLED] (by initiator)
- NEGOTIATING --> [REJECTED] --> [RE-NEGOTIATING] or [ARCHIVED]
- VALIDATED --> [INVALID] --> [REVISION_REQUIRED]
- EXECUTING --> [DISPUTED] --> [ARBITRATION] --> [RESOLVED] or [TERMINATED]

5.3 Platform Capabilities
Capability
Multi-Party Matching
Win-Win Validation
Flexible Negotiation
Milestone Tracking
Trust & Reputation
Domain Adaptability

Description
Algorithmic matching of compatible
Suppliers, Consumers, and Enhancers
Mathematical/model-based validation that all
parties benefit
Multi-round, asynchronous negotiation with
proposal versioning
Progress tracking with conditional payment
releases
Rating, review, and reputation scoring across
all party types
Configurable deal templates, resource types,
and value models

5.2 Service Catalog

5.2.1 User & Identity Service
Responsibility: Authentication, authorization, identity verification (KYC), session
management, MFA
Aspect

Details

Service ID
Team Ownership
Deployment
Data Ownership

user-identity-svc

Platform Security
3+ instances, critical path
Users, credentials, KYC data, sessions, MFA
tokens

Data Model:
User {
user_id: UUID (PK)
email: String (unique, encrypted)
phone: String (encrypted)
password_hash: String (bcrypt)
status: Enum [PENDING_VERIFICATION, ACTIVE, SUSPENDED, DEACTIVATED]
email_verified: Boolean
phone_verified: Boolean
kyc_status: Enum [NOT_REQUIRED, PENDING, VERIFIED, FAILED, EXPIRED]
mfa_enabled: Boolean
created_at: Timestamp
updated_at: Timestamp
}
UserProfile {
profile_id: UUID (PK)
user_id: UUID (FK)
display_name: String
avatar_url: String
locale: String
timezone: String
notification_preferences: JSON
}

KYCRecord {
kyc_id: UUID (PK)
user_id: UUID (FK)
provider: String (e.g., "onfido", "jumio")
provider_reference: String
status: Enum
document_type: String
verification_result: JSON
completed_at: Timestamp
}

APIs (REST + gRPC):
REST APIs:
POST /api/v1/auth/register
POST /api/v1/auth/login
POST /api/v1/auth/logout
POST /api/v1/auth/refresh
POST /api/v1/auth/mfa/enable
POST /api/v1/auth/mfa/verify
GET /api/v1/auth/me
PUT /api/v1/users/{id}/profile
POST /api/v1/users/{id}/kyc/initiate
GET /api/v1/users/{id}/kyc/status
gRPC Services:
service IdentityService {
rpc Authenticate(TokenRequest) returns (UserIdentity);
rpc Authorize(PermissionRequest) returns (AuthorizationResult);
rpc ValidateSession(SessionRequest) returns (SessionValidity);
rpc GetUserBulk(UserIdList) returns (UserList);
}

Events Published:
- user.registered
- user.activated
- user.suspended
- user.deactivated
- user.kyc.completed
- user.kyc.failed
- user.login.succeeded
- user.login.failed
- user.mfa.enabled

Technology Stack: - Runtime: Node.js / Go - Database: PostgreSQL (users), Redis
(sessions/cache) - Auth: OAuth2/OIDC, JWT (RS256), bcrypt - KYC: Onfido/Jumio
integration

5.2.2 Party & Profile Service
Responsibility: Party CRUD, party composition, role management, party relationships,
verification status

Aspect

Details

Service ID
Team Ownership
Deployment
Data Ownership

party-profile-svc

Core Platform
2+ instances
Parties, party_members, party_roles,
party_relationships, verifications

Key Concepts: - A Party is an entity (individual or organization) that participates in deals - A
Party has a Type: SUPPLIER, CONSUMER, ENHANCER, or MULTI (can play multiple
roles) - A Party consists of one or more Members (users or sub-entities) - Parties can have
Relationships (parent-child, partnership, etc.)
Data Model:
Party {
party_id: UUID (PK)
party_type: Enum [SUPPLIER, CONSUMER, ENHANCER, MULTI]
entity_type: Enum [INDIVIDUAL, ORGANIZATION, GROUP]
display_name: String
description: Text
status: Enum [DRAFT, ACTIVE, SUSPENDED, VERIFIED, INACTIVE]
verification_level: Enum [NONE, BASIC, VERIFIED, PREMIUM]
metadata: JSON (domain-specific attributes)
created_by: UUID (User FK)
created_at: Timestamp
updated_at: Timestamp
}
PartyMember {

State Machine Definition:

states:
- DRAFT
- PUBLISHED
- MATCHING
- NEGOTIATING
- VALIDATED
- APPROVED
- ACCEPTED
- AGREED
- SIGNED
- EXECUTING
- MILESTONE_REACHED
- COMPLETED
- SETTLED
- CLOSED
- CANCELLED
- REJECTED
- DISPUTED
- ARCHIVED
transitions:
- { from: DRAFT,
to: PUBLISHED,
event: deal.published,
auto: false }
- { from: DRAFT,
to: ARCHIVED,
event: deal.discarded,
auto: false }
- { from: PUBLISHED,
to: MATCHING,
event: deal.matching.started, auto: true
}
- { from: MATCHING,
to: NEGOTIATING, event: deal.parties.matched, auto: true
}
- { from: NEGOTIATING,
to: VALIDATED,
event: deal.terms.validated, auto: false
}
- { from: NEGOTIATING,
to: REJECTED,
event: deal.rejected,
auto: false }
- { from: REJECTED,
to: NEGOTIATING, event: deal.renegotiated,
auto: false }
- { from: REJECTED,
to: ARCHIVED,
event: deal.archived,
auto: false }
- { from: VALIDATED,
to: APPROVED,
event: deal.approved,
auto: false }
- { from: VALIDATED,
to: NEGOTIATING, event: deal.revision.required, auto:
false }
- { from: APPROVED,
to: ACCEPTED,
event: deal.accepted,
auto: false }
- { from: ACCEPTED,
to: AGREED,
event: deal.agreed,
auto: false }
- { from: AGREED,
to: SIGNED,
event: deal.signed,
auto: false }
- { from: SIGNED,
to: EXECUTING,
event: deal.execution.started, auto: true }
- { from: EXECUTING,
to: MILESTONE_REACHED, event: milestone.completed,
auto: true }
- { from: MILESTONE_REACHED, to: COMPLETED,
event: deal.all_milestones.done,
auto: true }
- { from: COMPLETED,
to: SETTLED,
event: deal.settled,
auto: true }
- { from: SETTLED,
to: CLOSED,
event: deal.closed,
auto: true }
- { from: EXECUTING,
to: DISPUTED,
event: deal.disputed,
auto: false }
- { from: DISPUTED,
to: EXECUTING,
event: dispute.resolved,
auto: false }
- { from: DISPUTED,
to: CANCELLED,
event: deal.terminated,
auto: false }
- { from: "*",
to: CANCELLED,
event: deal.cancelled,
auto: false }

APIs:

5.2.4 Matching & Discovery Service
Responsibility: Algorithmic matching of compatible parties, deal recommendations,
compatibility scoring
Aspect

Details

Service ID
Team Ownership
Deployment
Data Ownership

matching-svc

Data Science / Core Platform
2+ instances, background workers
Match_results, compatibility_scores,
matching_rules, recommendation_cache

Core Matching Algorithm:
For a given deal requiring parties [S, C, E]:
1. Filter candidates by: domain, location, availability, verification level
2. Score each candidate by: profile completeness, reputation, past performance
3. Compute pairwise compatibility: S<->C, S<->E, C<->E
4. Compute triple compatibility: win-win-win score
5. Rank candidate combinations by aggregate score
6. Apply diversity and fairness constraints
7. Return top-N recommendations with explanation

Data Model:
MatchResult {
match_id: UUID (PK)
deal_id: UUID (FK)
supplier_party_id: UUID (FK)
consumer_party_id: UUID (FK)
enhancer_party_id: UUID (FK)
overall_score: Float (0.0 - 1.0)
pairwise_scores: JSON {s_c: Float, s_e: Float, c_e: Float}
win_win_win_score: Float
match_reasons: JSON[]
status: Enum [PENDING_REVIEW, ACCEPTED, REJECTED, EXPIRED]
generated_at: Timestamp
reviewed_at: Timestamp (nullable)
}
CompatibilityScore {
score_id: UUID (PK)
party_a_id: UUID (FK)
party_b_id: UUID (FK)
score: Float
factors: JSON
computed_at: Timestamp
}
MatchingRule {
rule_id: UUID (PK)
domain: String

}

rule_type: Enum [FILTER, SCORE, EXCLUDE, REQUIRE]
condition: JSON
weight: Float
priority: Int
is_active: Boolean

APIs:
REST:
POST /api/v1/matching/find
# Find matches for a deal
GET /api/v1/matching/results/{matchId} # Get match details
POST /api/v1/matching/results/{matchId}/accept # Accept match
POST /api/v1/matching/results/{matchId}/reject # Reject match
GET /api/v1/matching/recommendations
# Get personalized recommendations
POST /api/v1/matching/refresh/{dealId} # Refresh matches for deal
GET /api/v1/matching/compatibility/{partyA}/{partyB} # Check compatibility
gRPC:
service MatchingService {
rpc FindMatches(MatchRequest) returns (MatchResultList);
rpc GetCompatibilityScore(CompatibilityRequest) returns (ScoreResult);
rpc ComputeWinWinWinScore(WinWinWinRequest) returns (ScoreResult);
rpc GetRecommendations(RecommendationRequest) returns (RecommendationList);
}

Events Published:
- matching.completed
- matching.match.accepted
- matching.match.rejected
- matching.recommendation.generated

Events Consumed:
- deal.published (triggers matching)
- deal.negotiation.started
- party.created (updates candidate pool)
- party.updated (updates candidate pool)

5.2.7 Value Distribution & Pricing Service
Responsibility: Value modeling, pricing algorithms, win-win validation, cost/benefit analysis,
dynamic pricing
Aspect

Details

Service ID
Team Ownership
Deployment

value-distribution-svc

Data Science / Core Platform
2+ instances

Aspect
Data Ownership

Details
Value_models, pricing_rules,
win_win_analyses, market_benchmarks

Win-Win Validation Engine:
Inputs:
- Supplier's cost structure and minimum acceptable return
- Consumer's maximum willingness to pay
- Enhancer's cost and desired margin
- External market benchmarks
Validation Checks:
1. Supplier surplus > 0 (receives more than reservation price)
2. Consumer surplus > 0 (pays less than maximum willingness)
3. Enhancer surplus > 0 (profitable participation)
4. Total surplus > 0 (deal creates value)
5. No party is worse off than outside option
6. Incentive compatibility (truthful reporting is dominant strategy)
Output:
- Win-win-win score (0.0 - 1.0)
- Individual surplus estimates
- Risk-adjusted value distribution
- Confidence intervals

Data Model:
ValueDistribution {
distribution_id: UUID (PK)
deal_id: UUID (FK)
status: Enum [DRAFT, VALIDATED, REJECTED, REVISED]
model_type: Enum [FIXED, REVENUE_SHARE, COST_PLUS, HYBRID, CUSTOM]
allocations: JSON [
{party_id: UUID, role: String, value_type: String, amount: Decimal, currency: String,
conditions: JSON}
]
win_win_analysis: JSON {
supplier_surplus: Decimal,
consumer_surplus: Decimal,
enhancer_surplus: Decimal,
total_surplus: Decimal,
confidence_score: Float,
risks: [...]
}
market_benchmarks_used: UUID[]
created_at: Timestamp
validated_at: Timestamp (nullable)
}
PricingRule {
rule_id: UUID (PK)
domain: String

rule_type: Enum [BASE_PRICE, PREMIUM, DISCOUNT, MINIMUM, MAXIMUM,
DYNAMIC]
condition: JSON
formula: String
priority: Int
is_active: Boolean
}
MarketBenchmark {
benchmark_id: UUID (PK)
domain: String

value: Decimal
unit: String

region: String
recorded_at: Timestamp
}

5.2.10 Payment/Settlement Service
Responsibility: Payment orchestration, escrow management, milestone-based releases,
settlement, refund handling
Aspect

Details

Service ID
Team Ownership
Deployment
Data Ownership

payment-svc

Payments / Core Platform
3+ instances, critical path
Payment_orders, escrow_accounts,
transactions, settlements, refunds,
payment_methods

Payment Flow:
1. Deal agreed -> Payment plan created
2. Consumer funds escrow -> Funds held in escrow
3. Milestone completed -> Release condition triggered
4. Value Distribution Service calculates release amount
5. Escrow release executed -> Funds distributed to Supplier & Enhancer
6. Final milestone -> Remaining funds released
7. Settlement record created -> Deal settled

Data Model:
PaymentPlan {
plan_id: UUID (PK)

deal_id: UUID (FK)
status: Enum [DRAFT, PENDING_FUNDING, FUNDED, EXECUTING, COMPLETED,
CANCELLED]
total_amount: Decimal
currency: String (ISO 4217)
escrow_account_id: String
consumer_party_id: UUID (FK)
installments: JSON [
{
milestone_id: UUID,
amount: Decimal,
recipient_party_id: UUID,
release_condition: String,
status: Enum [PENDING, RELEASED, FAILED]
}
]
created_at: Timestamp
updated_at: Timestamp
}
Transaction {
transaction_id: UUID (PK)
plan_id: UUID (FK)
transaction_type: Enum [DEPOSIT, ESCROW_HOLD, RELEASE, REFUND, FEE,
ADJUSTMENT]
amount: Decimal
currency: String
from_party_id: UUID (FK, nullable)
to_party_id: UUID (FK, nullable)
status: Enum [PENDING, PROCESSING, COMPLETED, FAILED, REVERSED]
provider: String (e.g., "stripe", "flutterwave")
provider_transaction_id: String
metadata: JSON
created_at: Timestamp
completed_at: Timestamp (nullable)
}
Settlement {
settlement_id: UUID (PK)
deal_id: UUID (FK)
status: Enum [PENDING, PROCESSING, SETTLED, FAILED]
total_settled: Decimal
breakdown: JSON [
{party_id: UUID, role: String, amount: Decimal, method: String}
]
settled_at: Timestamp (nullable)
}
PaymentMethod {
method_id: UUID (PK)
party_id: UUID (FK)
method_type: Enum [BANK_TRANSFER, MOBILE_MONEY, CARD, CRYPTO, WALLET]

}

provider: String
account_details: JSON (encrypted)
is_default: Boolean
is_verified: Boolean
created_at: Timestamp

APIs:

5.2.12 Trust & Reputation Service
Responsibility: Rating calculation, review management, reputation scoring, trust badges,
fraud detection signals
Aspect

Details

Service ID
Team Ownership
Deployment
Data Ownership

trust-reputation-svc

Platform / Trust & Safety
2+ instances
Reviews, ratings, reputation_scores,
trust_badges, fraud_signals

Reputation Score Calculation:
Composite Score = weighted_sum(
- Deal completion rate: 25%
- Average rating: 20%
- Review sentiment: 15%
- Response timeliness: 10%
- Verification level: 10%
- Platform tenure: 5%
- Dispute history: 5%
- Community contributions: 5%
- Recency weighting: (reviews in last 90 days get 2x weight)
)
Score ranges:
- 0.0 - 0.3: New / Low reputation
- 0.3 - 0.6: Building reputation
- 0.6 - 0.8: Good reputation
- 0.8 - 0.95: Excellent reputation
- 0.95 - 1.0: Top-tier reputation

Data Model:
Review {
review_id: UUID (PK)
deal_id: UUID (FK)
reviewer_party_id: UUID (FK)
reviewed_party_id: UUID (FK)
role_context: Enum [AS_SUPPLIER, AS_CONSUMER, AS_ENHANCER]
overall_rating: Int (1-5)
category_ratings: JSON {
communication: Int,
reliability: Int,
quality: Int,
fairness: Int,
timeliness: Int
}
review_text: Text (nullable)
is_anonymous: Boolean
is_verified: Boolean (verified by platform)
helpful_count: Int
status: Enum [PUBLISHED, HIDDEN, UNDER_REVIEW, REMOVED]
created_at: Timestamp
updated_at: Timestamp
}
ReputationScore {
score_id: UUID (PK)
party_id: UUID (FK)
overall_score: Float (0.0 - 1.0)
deal_completion_rate: Float
average_rating: Float
total_reviews: Int
positive_reviews: Int
neutral_reviews: Int
negative_reviews: Int
detailed_scores: JSON
score_history: JSON[]
trust_badges: String[]
computed_at: Timestamp
}
TrustBadge {
badge_id: UUID (PK)
name: String
description: String
icon_url: String
criteria: JSON
is_active: Boolean
}

APIs:

REST:

# Submit review

# Get party reviews

# Get reputation score
GET /api/v1/parties/{partyId}/trust-badges
# Get trust badges

# Mark as helpful

# List reviews (admin)

5.2 Synchronous Communication

REST APIs (External-Facing)

Standards:
- OpenAPI 3.1 specification for all APIs
- JSON:API or standard REST conventions
- HTTP status codes: 200, 201, 204, 400, 401, 403, 404, 409, 422, 429, 500
- Pagination: cursor-based for large collections
- Versioning: URL path (/api/v1/, /api/v2/)
- Rate limiting: 100 req/min anonymous, 1000 req/min authenticated
- Request ID: X-Request-ID header for tracing
- Content negotiation: Accept/Content-Type headers
- CORS: Configured per environment
- HATEOAS: Optional, for discoverability

gRPC APIs (Internal Services)

// Internal service communication schema
syntax = "proto3";
package dealplatform.common;

// Shared types

message UUID {
string value = 1;
}
message Timestamp {
int64 seconds = 1;
int32 nanos = 2;
}

message Money {
string currency_code = 1;
int64 units = 2;
int32 nanos = 3;
}
message PaginationRequest {
int32 page_size = 1;
string page_token = 2;
}
message PaginationResponse {
string next_page_token = 1;
int32 total_count = 2;
}

// Error handling

message ServiceError {
string code = 1;
string message = 2;
map<string, string> details = 3;
}

gRPC Service Definitions per domain: - dealplatform.identity.v1 - Identity operations dealplatform.party.v1 - Party management - dealplatform.deal.v1 - Deal lifecycle dealplatform.payment.v1 - Payment operations - dealplatform.matching.v1 - Matching &
recommendations
Service Mesh Integration: - All gRPC traffic routed through service mesh (Istio/Linkerd) Automatic mTLS between services - Circuit breaking at the mesh level - Distributed tracing
headers propagated

"event_id": "evt_a1b2c3d4e5f6",

saga:
name: deal_creation
version: "1.0"
steps:
- name: create_deal
service: deal-mgmt-svc
action: CreateDeal
compensation: ArchiveDeal
- name: register_resources
service: resource-catalog-svc
action: RegisterResources
compensation: DeregisterResources
depends_on: [create_deal]
- name: create_value_distribution
service: value-distribution-svc
action: CreateDistribution
compensation: DeleteDistribution
depends_on: [create_deal]
- name: validate_win_win
service: value-distribution-svc
action: ValidateWinWin
compensation: null # no-op, validation is read-only
depends_on: [create_value_distribution]
- name: initialize_negotiation
service: negotiation-svc
action: StartNegotiation
compensation: EndNegotiation
depends_on: [create_value_distribution]
completion:
publish_event: deal.creation.completed
failure_policy:
max_retries: 3
retry_delay: "5s"
compensation_order: REVERSE
timeout: "30s"

Requirement

How Event Sourcing Helps

Complete audit trail
State reconstruction
Regulatory compliance
Dispute resolution
Analytics & ML
Debugging

Every state change is an immutable event
Rebuild any deal state at any point in time
Immutable record of all decisions and changes

ON deal_events(aggregate_type, aggregate_id, sequence_number);

CREATE TABLE deal_events_2024_01 PARTITION OF deal_events
FOR VALUES FROM ('2024-01-01') TO ('2024-02-01');

5.2.3 Deal Aggregate Reconstruction

// Event-sourced aggregate reconstruction

class DealAggregate {
private events: DomainEvent[] = [];
private snapshot: DealSnapshot | null = null;
private state: DealState;
async reconstruct(dealId: UUID): Promise<DealState> {

// 1. Get latest snapshot

this.snapshot = await snapshotStore.getLatest(dealId);
const fromSequence = this.snapshot ? this.snapshot.sequenceNumber : 0;

// 2. Get events after snapshot

this.events = await eventStore.getEvents(dealId, fromSequence);

// 3. Apply snapshot state if exists

if (this.snapshot) {
this.state = DealState.fromSnapshot(this.snapshot.data);
} else {
this.state = new DealState();
}

// 4. Apply events sequentially

for (const event of this.events) {
this.state.apply(event);
}

}

return this.state;

async appendEvent(event: DomainEvent): Promise<void> {

// Validate event against current state

const validation = this.state.validateTransition(event);
if (!validation.valid) {
throw new InvalidTransitionError(validation.reason);
}

// Append to event store

await eventStore.append(event);

// Apply to state

this.state.apply(event);

// Check if snapshot needed (every 100 events)

}

}

if (this.events.length % 100 === 0) {
await snapshotStore.save(this.aggregateId, this.state.toSnapshot());
}

5.3.2 Analytics Read Model (ClickHouse)
-- Deal events table for analytics

CREATE TABLE deal_analytics_events (
event_id UUID,
event_type String,
deal_id UUID,
deal_domain String,
deal_status String,
party_ids Array(UUID),
event_timestamp DateTime64(3),
event_date Date DEFAULT toDate(event_timestamp),

-- Value metrics

deal_value Decimal(18, 2),
currency String,

-- Performance metrics

processing_time_ms UInt32,

-- Dimensions

region String,
platform_version String
) ENGINE = MergeTree()
ORDER BY (event_date, deal_domain, event_type)
PARTITION BY toYYYYMM(event_date);

-- Aggregated metrics materialized view

CREATE MATERIALIZED VIEW deal_metrics_mv
ENGINE = SummingMergeTree()
ORDER BY (event_date, deal_domain, deal_status)
AS SELECT
event_date,
deal_domain,
deal_status,
count() as deal_count,
sum(deal_value) as total_value,
avg(processing_time_ms) as avg_processing_time
FROM deal_analytics_events
GROUP BY event_date, deal_domain, deal_status;

5.2 External Payment Providers

Payment Provider Adapter

// Abstract payment provider interface

interface PaymentProvider {
name: string;
supportedMethods: PaymentMethod[];

supportedCurrencies: string[];

// Core operations

initializePayment(request: PaymentRequest): Promise<PaymentInitialization>;
processPayment(paymentId: string): Promise<PaymentResult>;
verifyPayment(paymentId: string): Promise<PaymentVerification>;
refund(request: RefundRequest): Promise<RefundResult>;

// Escrow operations

createEscrow(dealId: string, amount: Money): Promise<EscrowAccount>;
releaseEscrow(escrowId: string, distribution: Distribution[]): Promise<ReleaseResult>;

// Webhook handling
}

handleWebhook(payload: unknown, signature: string): Promise<WebhookEvent>;

// Provider implementations

class StripeProvider implements PaymentProvider { ... }
class FlutterwaveProvider implements PaymentProvider { ... }
class MPesaProvider implements PaymentProvider { ... }
class CryptoWalletProvider implements PaymentProvider { ... }

// Provider factory

class PaymentProviderFactory {
getProvider(method: PaymentMethod, currency: string): PaymentProvider {
}

}

// Strategy: select best provider based on method + currency + region

Payment Integration Architecture:

Idempotency Pattern:
// All payment operations are idempotent

async processPayment(request: PaymentRequest): Promise<PaymentResult> {
const idempotencyKey = request.idempotencyKey ||
generateKey(request.dealId, request.amount, request.currency);

// Check if already processed

const existing = await this.transactionStore.getByIdempotencyKey(idempotencyKey);
if (existing) {
return { status: 'already_processed', transactionId: existing.id };

}

// Acquire distributed lock

const lock = await this.lockManager.acquire(`payment:${idempotencyKey}`, 30);
try {

// Process with provider

const result = await this.provider.process(request);

// Record transaction

await this.transactionStore.save({
idempotencyKey,
...result
});

}

return result;
} finally {
await lock.release();
}

5.3 KYC/Identity Verification
KYC Integration Flow:
1. User initiates KYC in app
2. Platform calls KYC Adapter with user info
3. Adapter selects provider (Onfido/Jumio) based on region
4. Provider generates SDK token for client-side capture
5. User captures ID document + selfie (client-side)
6. Provider processes verification (async)
7. Provider sends webhook with result
8. KYC Adapter processes webhook
9. User & Identity Service updates KYC status
10. Event published: user.kyc.completed
11. Party & Profile Service may upgrade verification level
12. Search Service updates index

KYC Provider Adapter:
interface KYCProvider {
createCheck(userId: UUID, documents: DocumentInfo[]): Promise<KYCCheck>;
getCheckStatus(checkId: string): Promise<KYCStatus>;
handleWebhook(payload: unknown): Promise<KYCResult>;
getSupportedDocuments(country: string): Promise<DocumentType[]>;
}

5.4 Document Signing (E-Signatures)
E-Signature Integration Flow:
1. Deal reaches AGREED state
2. Agreement Service generates contract from template
3. Agreement Service calls E-Signature Adapter
4. Adapter creates envelope with DocuSign/HelloSign

5. Signing URLs generated for each party
6. Parties redirected to signing ceremony
7. Signatures captured by provider
8. Webhook received on completion
9. Agreement Service updates signature records
10. When all signed -> event: deal.signed
11. Deal Management advances to SIGNED state

Notification Routing:
interface NotificationRouter {
route(notification: Notification): Promise<Channel[]> {
const channels: Channel[] = [];

// 1. Check user preferences

const prefs = await this.preferenceService.get(notification.userId);

// 2. Apply priority-based routing

switch (notification.priority) {
case 'URGENT':
channels.push('in_app', 'push', 'sms', 'email');
break;
case 'HIGH':
channels.push('in_app', 'push', 'email');
if (prefs.smsForHighPriority) channels.push('sms');
break;
case 'NORMAL':
channels.push('in_app');
if (prefs.emailEnabled) channels.push('email');
break;
case 'LOW':
if (prefs.emailEnabled) channels.push('email');
break;
}

// 3. Apply quiet hours

if (prefs.quietHours.enabled) {

}

channels = this.filterQuietHours(channels, prefs.quietHours);

// 4. Apply channel availability
}

}

return channels.filter(c => prefs.channelEnabled(c));

5.2 Caching Strategy

Multi-Layer Caching

+-----------------------------------------------------------+
|
CLIENT CACHE
|
| - Browser/APP: HTTP cache headers, local storage
| - TTL: varies per resource type
|
+-----------------------------------------------------------+
|
+-----------------------------------------------------------+
|
CDN CACHE (CloudFlare)
|
| - Static assets: images, documents, public APIs
|
| - TTL: 1h for semi-static, 24h for static
|
| - Cache keys: URL + Accept-Language
|
+-----------------------------------------------------------+

|

|
+-----------------------------------------------------------+
|
API GATEWAY CACHE
|
| - Rate limit counters, auth tokens
|
| - TTL: 5min for auth, 1min for rate limits
|
+-----------------------------------------------------------+
|
+-----------------------------------------------------------+
|
SERVICE-LEVEL CACHE
|
| - Redis Cluster with sharding
|
| - Cache patterns: Cache-Aside, Write-Through
| - TTL: 10min for deals, 1h for profiles
|
| - Cache invalidation via events
|
+-----------------------------------------------------------+
|
+-----------------------------------------------------------+
|
DATABASE CACHE
|
| - PostgreSQL shared_buffers, query cache
| - Connection pool: 10-50 per service instance
+-----------------------------------------------------------+

|

|
|

Cache Key Strategy

Pattern: {entity_type}:{entity_id}:{aspect}:{version}
Examples:
- deal:dl_abc123:summary:v1
- party:pt_xyz789:profile:v1
- party:pt_xyz789:reputation:v2
- resource:rs_def456:availability:2024-01-15
- search:results:deals:agriculture:kenya:{hash_of_params}

Cache Invalidation
Invalidation Strategy

Use Case

Implementation

TTL-based

Non-critical,
eventually
consistent data
Critical data that
must be fresh
Data that
changes
infrequently
Admin
operations

Redis EXPIRE

Event-based
Write-through

Explicit purge
// Event-based cache invalidation

class CacheInvalidationListener {
@OnEvent('deal.updated')
async handleDealUpdated(event: DealUpdatedEvent) {
const keys = [
`deal:${event.dealId}:summary:*`,
`deal:${event.dealId}:details:*`,
`search:results:deals:*`, // Invalidate search caches

Listen to Kafka events
Update cache on write

Direct Redis DEL

];

}

}

for (const pattern of keys) {
await this.redis.delPattern(pattern);
}

5.4 Circuit Breaker Pattern
// Circuit breaker configuration per dependency

interface CircuitBreakerConfig {
failureThreshold: number;
// Open after N failures
successThreshold: number;
// Close after N successes
timeoutDuration: number;
// Request timeout (ms)
resetTimeout: number;
// Time before half-open (ms)
halfOpenMaxCalls: number;
// Max calls in half-open state

}
const defaultCBConfig: CircuitBreakerConfig = {
failureThreshold: 5,
successThreshold: 3,
timeoutDuration: 10000,
resetTimeout: 30000,
halfOpenMaxCalls: 3,
};

// Service-specific configurations

const serviceCBConfigs: Record<string, CircuitBreakerConfig> = {
'payment-svc': { ...defaultCBConfig, timeoutDuration: 15000, resetTimeout: 60000 },
'kyc-provider': { ...defaultCBConfig, failureThreshold: 3, resetTimeout: 120000 },
'email-provider': { ...defaultCBConfig, failureThreshold: 10 },
};

Circuit Breaker States:
[CLOSED] --(5 failures)--> [OPEN] --(30s timeout)--> [HALF_OPEN]
^
|
|
|
+------------(3 successes)-------------------------------+
CLOSED: Normal operation, requests pass through
OPEN: Fast-fail, return cached response or error
HALF_OPEN: Limited requests allowed to test recovery

5.5 Bulkhead Pattern

bulkheads:
deal-mgmt-svc:
max_concurrent_calls: 100
max_wait_duration: 5s
payment-svc:
max_concurrent_calls: 50 # Lower for critical financial operations
max_wait_duration: 10s
matching-svc:
max_concurrent_calls: 200 # Higher for read-heavy operations
max_wait_duration: 2s
notification-svc:
max_concurrent_calls: 300
max_wait_duration: 1s

5.1.3 Authorization Model (RBAC + ABAC)
Role-Based Access Control (RBAC):
Role

Permissions

guest

Read public deals, search
Create deals, manage own profile, negotiate
All user + publish deals, accept matches
All verified + advanced analytics, priority matching
Manage party members, resources, deals for party
Full party control, billing, deletion
Review content, resolve disputes, suspend users
Full platform access, configuration, audit
Internal service-to-service communication

user
verified_user
premium_user
party_admin
party_owner
moderator
admin
system

Attribute-Based Access Control (ABAC):
policies:
- name: deal_access
description: Users can only access deals they participate in
resource: deal
action: [read, update]
condition: |
subject.party_ids contains resource.participant_party_ids
OR subject.roles contains 'admin'
OR subject.roles contains 'moderator'
- name: negotiation_write
description: Only deal participants can submit proposals
resource: negotiation_session
action: [submit_proposal, accept, reject]
condition: |
subject.party_ids contains resource.participating_party_ids
- name: payment_access
description: Users can only view payments for their deals

resource: payment_plan
action: [read]
condition: |
subject.party_ids contains resource.payer_party_id
OR subject.party_ids contains resource.payee_party_ids
- name: admin_override
description: Admins can access everything
resource: '*'
action: '*'
condition: |
subject.roles contains 'admin'

Policy Engine (OPA - Open Policy Agent):
package dealplatform.authz
import future.keywords.if
import future.keywords.in
default allow := false
allow if {
input.user.roles[_] == "admin"
}
allow if {
input.action == "read"
input.resource.type == "deal"
input.user.party_ids[_] == input.resource.party_ids[_]
}
allow if {
input.action in ["update", "delete"]
input.resource.type == "party"
input.user.user_id == input.resource.owner_id
}

// PII fields encrypted at application level
@Entity()
class User {
@PrimaryColumn('uuid')
userId: string;

@Column({
transformer: new FieldEncryptionTransformer('email')
})
email: string; // Encrypted in DB
@Column({
transformer: new FieldEncryptionTransformer('phone')
})
phone: string; // Encrypted in DB
@Column()
@Index()
emailHash: string; // HMAC for lookup without decryption

}

@Column()
@Index()
phoneHash: string; // HMAC for lookup
