8.5 Validation Decision Tree

graph TD
A[Deal Proposal Submitted] --> B{Rule 1:<br/>All Gains > 0?}
B -->|No| C[BLOCK: Critical<br/>Party would lose]
B -->|Yes| D{Rule 2:<br/>All Shares ≤ 70%?}
D -->|No| E[BLOCK: Critical<br/>Exploitation risk]
D -->|Yes| F{Rule 5:<br/>Consumer sees value?}
F -->|No| G[FLAG: Consumer value<br/>proposition weak]
F -->|Yes| H{Rule 4:<br/>Enhancer fee fair?}
H -->|No| I[FLAG: Adjust enhancer<br/>compensation]
H -->|Yes| J{Rule 3:<br/>All Shares ≥ 10%?}
J -->|No| K[FLAG: Low share risk]<br/>L --> M[Proceed to<br/>Fairness Scoring]
K --> L[Require Acknowledgment]
G --> N[Suggest Adjustments]
I --> N
L --> M
N --> O[Party revises offer]
O --> A
M --> P{Fairness Score?}
P -->|≥ 0.90| Q[Status: EXCELLENT]
P -->|≥ 0.70| R[Status: GOOD]
P -->|≥ 0.50| S[Status: FAIR<br/>Recommend improvement]
P -->|< 0.50| T[Status: POOR<br/>Requires renegotiation]
Q --> U[Available for Signing]
R --> U
S --> V[Available with Warning]
T --> W[Not Available - Revise]
W --> O

8.6 Pseudocode: Win-Win-Win Validation Engine
class WinWinWinValidator:

def __init__(self, domain_config):
self.max_share = 0.70
self.min_share = 0.10
self.min_deal_size = domain_config.min_deal_size
self.discount_rate = domain_config.discount_rate
def validate_deal(self, deal) -> ValidationResult:

"""
Main validation entry point.
Returns: ValidationResult with status, score, and detailed feedback.
"""
# Step 1: Normalize all values to PVE
pve_result = self._normalize_to_pve(deal)

# Step 2: Check critical rules (hard blocks)

critical_checks = self._check_critical_rules(pve_result)
if not critical_checks.all_passed:
return ValidationResult(
status=DealStatus.BLOCKED,
fairness_score=0.0,
violations=critical_checks.violations
)

# Step 3: Check warning rules (flags)

warning_checks = self._check_warning_rules(pve_result)

# Step 4: Calculate fairness score

fairness_score = self._calculate_fairness_score(pve_result)

# Step 5: Generate party-specific feedback

feedback = self._generate_feedback(pve_result, fairness_score)

# Step 6: Determine final status

status = self._determine_status(fairness_score, warning_checks)
return ValidationResult(
status=status,
fairness_score=fairness_score,
pve_breakdown=pve_result,
violations=critical_checks.violations,
warnings=warning_checks.warnings,
party_feedback=feedback
)
def _normalize_to_pve(self, deal) -> PVEResult:

"""Convert all value types to Present Value Equivalent."""

consumer_pve = self._calculate_party_pve(deal.consumer_value)
supplier_pve = self._calculate_party_pve(deal.supplier_value)
enhancer_pve = self._calculate_party_pve(deal.enhancer_value)
platform_fee = self._calculate_platform_fee(deal)
tdv = consumer_pve + supplier_pve + enhancer_pve + platform_fee
return PVEResult(
consumer_pve=consumer_pve,
supplier_pve=supplier_pve,
enhancer_pve=enhancer_pve,
platform_fee=platform_fee,
total_deal_value=tdv
)
def _check_critical_rules(self, pve) -> CriticalCheckResult:
violations = []

# Rule 1: Positive gain for all

for party in ['consumer', 'supplier', 'enhancer']:
gain = pve.get_gain(party)
if gain <= 0:
violations.append(Violation(
rule="R1_POSITIVE_GAIN",
party=party,
message=f"{party} has non-positive gain: {gain}"
))

# Rule 2: Max share ≤ 70%

for party in ['consumer', 'supplier', 'enhancer']:
share = pve.get_share(party)
if share > self.max_share:
violations.append(Violation(
rule="R2_MAX_SHARE",
party=party,
message=f"{party} share {share:.1%} exceeds 70% limit"
))

# Rule 5: Consumer value proposition

consumer_cost = pve.consumer_contribution
alt_cost = pve.consumer_alternative_cost
if consumer_cost >= alt_cost * 0.95:
violations.append(Violation(
rule="R5_CONSUMER_VALUE",
party="consumer",
message="Consumer cost
or exceeds independent sourcing"
))

接近

# Rule 6: Minimum deal size

if pve.total_deal_value < self.min_deal_size:
violations.append(Violation(
rule="R6_MIN_DEAL_SIZE",
party="all",
message=f"Deal value ${pve.total_deal_value} below minimum"
))
return CriticalCheckResult(
all_passed=len(violations) == 0,
violations=violations
)
def _calculate_fairness_score(self, pve) -> float:

"""Calculate composite fairness score."""
# Dimension 1: Absolute gain (0-1)

gains = [pve.get_gain(p) for p in ['consumer', 'supplier', 'enhancer']]
min_gain = min(gains)
max_gain = max(gains)
if max_gain <= 0:
absolute_score = 0.0
else:

# Normalized: all positive = 1.0, one at zero = 0.0

absolute_score = max(0.0, min(gains)) / (max_gain * 0.5)
absolute_score = min(1.0, absolute_score)

# Dimension 2: Proportional fairness (Gini-inspired)

shares = [pve.get_share(p) for p in ['consumer', 'supplier', 'enhancer']]
mean_share = sum(shares) / 3
variance = sum((s - mean_share)**2 for s in shares) / 3
proportional_score = max(0.0, 1.0 - variance * 10)

# Dimension 3: Market benchmark

benchmark_scores = []
for party in ['consumer', 'supplier', 'enhancer']:
premium = pve.get_benchmark_premium(party)

# Score = 1.0 at 0% premium, decreases as deviates

benchmark_scores.append(max(0.0, 1.0 - abs(premium) * 2))
benchmark_score = sum(benchmark_scores) / 3

# Dimension 4: Opportunity cost

oc_scores = []
for party in ['consumer', 'supplier', 'enhancer']:
net_benefit = pve.get_net_benefit(party)
oc_scores.append(1.0 if net_benefit > 0 else max(0.0, 0.5 + net_benefit /
pve.get_oc(party)))
oc_score = sum(oc_scores) / 3

# Weighted composite

return (0.25 * absolute_score +
0.30 * proportional_score +
0.25 * benchmark_score +
0.20 * oc_score)
def generate_party_dashboard(self, party_id, deal) -> Dashboard:

"""Generate real-time negotiation dashboard for a party."""

pve = self._normalize_to_pve(deal)
fairness_score = self._calculate_fairness_score(pve)

gain = pve.get_gain(party_id)
share = pve.get_share(party_id)
market_premium = pve.get_benchmark_premium(party_id)
next_best = pve.get_next_best_alternative(party_id)
return Dashboard(
net_gain=gain,
share_percent=share * 100,
vs_market=market_premium,
vs_next_best=gain - next_best,
vs_do_nothing=gain,
fairness_score=fairness_score,
checks={
'gain_positive': gain > 0,
'share_in_bounds': self.min_share <= share <= self.max_share,

'beats_market': market_premium > 0,
'beats_alternative': gain > next_best

)

},
tips=self._generate_tips(party_id, deal, pve)

8.2 Model A: Fixed Price Model
Description: Consumer pays a predetermined fixed amount. Proceeds are split between
Supplier and Enhancer.
graph LR
C[Consumer<br/>Pays $10,000] --> PF[Platform Fee<br/>10% = $1,000]
PF --> SP[Supplier Pool<br/>$9,000]
SP --> S[Supplier<br/>60% = $5,400]
SP --> E[Enhancer<br/>30% = $2,700]
SP --> P[Platform<br/>Retention<br/>10% = $900]
style C fill:#e1f5fe
style S fill:#e8f5e9
style E fill:#fff3e0
style P fill:#fce4ec
style PF fill:#f3e5f5
style SP fill:#f3e5f5

Value Flow:

Consumer: Pays $10,000 → Receives output (crops worth $12,000 market)
Net Gain = $2,000 (20% savings vs market)
Supplier: Provides land (opportunity cost: $4,000)
Receives: $5,400
Net Gain = $1,400
Enhancer: Provides seeds, fertilizer, labor (cost: $2,000)
Receives: $2,700
Net Gain = $700
Platform: Facilitates match + escrow
Receives: $1,900 total ($1,000 from consumer + $900 from pool)
TDV = $2,000 + $1,400 + $700 = $4,100 (total value created)

Platform Fee Structure:
Base Fee: 8% of deal value (minimum $100)
Escrow Fee: 2% (waived for Platinum members)
Payment Processing: 1.5% (passed through)
Total Platform Revenue = $1,000 (10% effective rate)

Risk Allocation: | Risk | Allocation | Mitigation | |——|————|————| | Output quality |
Supplier/Enhancer | Escrow holdback (20% until verified) | | Non-payment | Consumer | Full
escrow upfront | | Non-delivery | Supplier/Enhancer | Reputation penalty + collateral | |
Market price change | Consumer | Fixed price = locked in |
When to Use: Standardized products, clear specifications, predictable costs, parties with
moderate trust.
8.3 Model B: Revenue Share Model
Description: Output is sold jointly and proceeds are distributed according to agreed
percentages. Creates ongoing partnerships.
graph TD
subgraph "Revenue Generation"
O[Output Produced] --> SALES[Sales Channel]
SALES --> REV[Total Revenue<br/>$15,000]
end
subgraph "Distribution Waterfall"
REV --> PF[Platform Fee<br/>8% = $1,200]
PF --> ESC[Escrow Reserve<br/>5% = $750]
ESC --> DIST[Distributable<br/>$13,050]
end
subgraph "Party Shares"
DIST --> S[Supplier<br/>50% = $6,525]
DIST --> E[Enhancer<br/>30% = $3,915]
DIST --> C[Consumer<br/>20% = $2,610]

end
subgraph "Reserve Release"
ESC -. Final accounting .-> R[Released proportionally<br/>after 90 days]
end
style REV fill:#e8f5e9
style S fill:#e8f5e9
style E fill:#fff3e0
style C fill:#e1f5fe

Revenue Share Formula:
Distributable_Revenue = Gross_Revenue × (1 - Platform_Fee% - Reserve%)
Party_Payout_P = Distributable_Revenue × Share_P
Standard Share Templates:
"Equal Partners": 33.3% / 33.3% / 33.4%
"Supplier Heavy": 50% / 30% / 20% (Supplier/Enhancer/Consumer)
"Enhancer Heavy": 30% / 50% / 20%
"Consumer Heavy": 30% / 30% / 40%
"Custom": Negotiated split

Dynamic Share Adjustment (for multi-period deals):
Share_P(t) = Base_Share_P + Performance_Adjustment_P(t)
Where Performance_Adjustment is based on:
- Supplier: Output quality, timeliness, yield
- Enhancer: Input quality, support, innovation
- Consumer: Sales performance, marketing effort
Adjustment bounded: ±10% of base share per period

Platform Fee Structure:
Revenue Share Fee: 8% of gross revenue (collected at sale)
Management Fee: $50/month for ongoing deals
Accounting/Reporting: Included
Platform Revenue = $1,200 (one-time) + $50/month × duration

Risk Allocation: | Risk | Allocation | Mitigation | |——|————|————| | Sales risk |
Shared (all parties lose if no sales) | Consumer incentivized to sell | | Production risk |
Supplier/Enhancer | Lower share if targets missed | | Price volatility | All parties | Reserve
fund buffer | | Deadlock | N/A | Pre-defined exit clauses |
When to Use: Joint ventures, ongoing relationships, uncertain market prices, aligned longterm incentives.

8.4 Model C: Cost-Plus Model
Description: Transparent cost build-up with agreed margin. Consumer sees full cost
breakdown.
graph TD
subgraph "Cost Stack"
SC[Supplier Cost<br/>Resource Value<br/>$4,000] --> TC[Total Cost Base]
EC[Enhancer Cost<br/>Inputs + Labor<br/>$3,500] --> TC
PC[Platform Cost<br/>Facilitation<br/>$500] --> TC
TC --> TC_TOT[Total Cost<br/>$8,000]
end
subgraph "Margin Application"
TC_TOT --> SM[Supplier Margin<br/>15% = $600]
TC_TOT --> EM[Enhancer Margin<br/>20% = $700]
TC_TOT --> PM[Platform Margin<br/>10% = $800]
end
subgraph "Consumer Price"
SM --> FP[Final Price<br/>$10,100]
EM --> FP
PM --> FP
TC_TOT --> FP
end
style TC_TOT fill:#fff9c4
style FP fill:#e8f5e9

Cost-Plus Formula:
Final_Price = (Supplier_Cost + Enhancer_Cost + Platform_Cost) × (1 + Total_Margin%)
Where:
Total_Margin% = (Supplier_Margin + Enhancer_Margin + Platform_Margin)
/ Total_Cost × 100
Party_Payout_P = Cost_P × (1 + Margin_P%)
Platform Fee is included in the cost stack AND takes margin.

Transparent Cost Breakdown (visible to Consumer):

Platform Fee Structure:
Included in cost stack: $500 facilitation cost
Plus margin share: $500 (10% on $500 cost, or ~5% of total)
Total Platform Revenue: ~$1,000 (9.9% effective)

Risk Allocation: | Risk | Allocation | Mitigation | |——|————|————| | Cost overrun |
Supplier/Enhancer | Pre-approved cost ceiling | | Scope creep | Consumer | Change order
process | | Inflation | All | Cost adjustment clause | | Audit | Platform | Random cost

When to Use: Custom projects, cost-sensitive consumers, high-trust relationships,
government/corporate procurement.
8.5 Model D: Barter/Exchange Model
Description: Non-monetary exchange of resources, services, and outputs. Platform provides
valuation guidance.
graph LR
subgraph "What Each Party Gives"
S[Supplier] --> SG[Idle Land<br/>6 months]
E[Enhancer] --> EG[Seeds + Expertise<br/>Value: $3,000]
C[Consumer] --> CG[Processing Equipment<br/>Access + Storage]
end
subgraph "What Each Party Receives"
S --> SR[40% of Crop Output<br/>+ Processing Service]
E --> ER[35% of Crop Output<br/>+ Land Access for R&D]
C --> CR[25% of Crop Output<br/>+ Premium Quality Assurance]

end
subgraph "Platform Role"
P[Platform] --> PV[Valuation Service]
P --> PE[Escrow of Non-Monetary Assets]
P --> PD[Dispute Resolution]
end
style S fill:#e8f5e9
style E fill:#fff3e0
style C fill:#e1f5fe

Barter Valuation Framework:
For each barter item I from party P:
Fair_Market_Value_I = Platform_Appraised_Value(I)
Validation:
|Party_P contributions| ≈ |Party_P receipts| ± 20%
If imbalance > 20%:
→ Suggest cash adjustment or additional barter items
Monetary_Equivalent = Σ Fair_Market_Value_I for all items

Platform Fee Structure:
Valuation Service: $100 per item appraised
Escrow (non-monetary): 5% of appraised value (minimum $200)
Matching Fee: $250 flat
Total Platform Revenue: ~$550-800 per deal

When to Use: Cash-constrained parties, complementary resources, mutual benefit scenarios,
developing markets.
8.6 Model E: Hybrid Model
Description: Combines multiple payment structures for complex deals. Most flexible model.
graph TD
subgraph "Hybrid Payment Structure"
subgraph "Phase 1: Upfront"
C1[Consumer] --> UP[Upfront Payment<br/>$5,000]
UP --> S1[Supplier<br/>$3,000]
UP --> E1[Enhancer<br/>$1,500]
UP --> P1[Platform<br/>$500]
end
subgraph "Phase 2: Milestone"
C2[Consumer] --> M1[Milestone 1<br/>Planting Complete<br/>$2,000]
C2 --> M2[Milestone 2<br/>Harvest Complete<br/>$3,000]
M1 --> SPLIT1[Split 50/30/20<br/>S/E/Platform]

M2 --> SPLIT2[Split 50/30/20<br/>S/E/Platform]
end
subgraph "Phase 3: Revenue Share"
SALES[Sales] --> REV[Revenue<br/>$15,000]
REV --> PF[Platform 8%]
PF --> RS[Revenue Split<br/>40% S / 35% E / 25% C]
end
end
style C1 fill:#e1f5fe
style C2 fill:#e1f5fe
style S1 fill:#e8f5e9
style E1 fill:#fff3e0
style RS fill:#f3e5f5

Hybrid Structure Formula:
Total_Deal = Upfront_Component + Milestone_Component + RevenueShare_Component
Where:
Upfront_Component = Fixed amount for immediate costs
Milestone_Component = Σ (Milestone_Payment_i × Achievement_i)
RevenueShare_Component = (Gross_Revenue - Threshold) × Share%
Each component can use different distribution models.
Platform fee varies by component:
- Upfront: 10%
- Milestone: 8%
- Revenue share: 6%

Milestone Definition:
Milestone = {
id: string,
description: string,
trigger_condition: "objective_verifiable_event",
verification_method: "oracle" | "party_consensus" | "third_party",
payment_amount: number,
payment_split: {supplier: %, enhancer: %, platform: %},
deadline: date,
penalty_for_miss: number # % reduction for late completion
}

When to Use: Complex multi-phase projects, high-value deals, parties with different risk
profiles, innovation partnerships.
8.7 Model Selection Decision Tree

graph TD
A[Deal Negotiation Begins] --> Q1{Is cash<br/>available?}
Q1 -->|No| B[Barter/Exchange Model]
Q1 -->|Yes| Q2{Ongoing relationship<br/>or one-time?}

Q2 -->|One-time| Q3{Need cost<br/>transparency?}
Q2 -->|Ongoing| Q4{Revenue easily<br/>measurable?}
Q3 -->|Yes| C[Cost-Plus Model]
Q3 -->|No| D[Fixed Price Model]
Q4 -->|Yes| E[Revenue Share Model]
Q4 -->|No| Q5{Multiple phases<br/>or milestones?}
Q5 -->|Yes| F[Hybrid Model]
Q5 -->|No| G[Default to Fixed Price<br/>with performance bonus]
B --> H[Platform assists<br/>with valuation]
C --> I[Consumer approves<br/>cost breakdown]
D --> J[Standard terms<br/>negotiation]
E --> K[Define revenue<br/>measurement]
F --> L[Define milestones<br/>and triggers]
G --> J

8. Pricing & Fee Mechanism
8.1 Platform Fee Architecture
The platform uses a tiered, dynamic fee structure that balances accessibility with
sustainability.
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
─┐
│
PLATFORM FEE STRUCTURE
│
├────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────┤
│
│
│ BASE FEE (applied to all deals)
│
│ ├── Matching Fee: 2% of deal value
│
│ ├── Escrow Fee: 1.5% of amount held
│
│ └── Payment Processing: 1% (pass-through to processor) │
│
Base Total: 4.5%
│
│
│
│ SUCCESS FEE (only on completed deals)
│
│ ├── Standard: 4% of deal value
│
│ ├── Complex deals: 6%
│
│ └── Repeat deals: 2.5%
│
│
│
│ EFFECTIVE RATES
│
│ ├── First-time simple deal: 8.5%
│
│ ├── First-time complex deal: 10.5%
│
│ └── Repeat simple deal: 7%
│
│
│
│ MINIMUMS
│
│ ├── Absolute minimum: $50
│
│ └── Minimum by domain: varies ($100-$500)
│
│
│

└────────────────────────────────────────
─────────────────┘

8.2 Dynamic Pricing Formula

Platform_Fee% = Base_Fee% × Trust_Multiplier × Complexity_Multiplier ×
Volume_Discount × Domain_Adjustment
Where:
Base_Fee% = 8.5% (standard rate)
Trust_Multiplier = f(min_trust_score_among_parties)
Trust >= 90 (Platinum): 0.80 (20% discount)
Trust >= 75 (Gold): 0.90 (10% discount)
Trust >= 60 (Silver): 1.00 (standard)
Trust >= 40 (Bronze): 1.15 (15% premium)
Trust < 40:
1.35 (35% premium + escrow required)
Complexity_Multiplier = f(deal_complexity_score)
Simple (fixed price, standard terms): 0.90
Medium (milestones, custom terms):
1.00
Complex (hybrid, multi-party, long-term): 1.25
Volume_Discount = f(monthly_deal_volume_for_party)
1-2 deals/month: 1.00
3-5 deals/month: 0.95 (5% discount)
6-10 deals/month: 0.90 (10% discount)
11+ deals/month: 0.85 (15% discount)
Domain_Adjustment = domain_specific_rate
Agriculture: 1.00
Manufacturing: 1.10
Technology:
0.95
Services:
1.05
Real Estate: 1.20

Example Calculation:
Deal: Agricultural produce, $10,000
Parties: Supplier (Trust 82/Gold), Consumer (Trust 65/Silver), Enhancer (Trust 70/Silver)
Complexity: Medium (milestone-based)
Consumer volume: 4 deals/month
Trust_Multiplier = min(0.90, 1.00, 1.00) = 0.90
Complexity_Multiplier = 1.00
Volume_Discount = 0.95 (Consumer's volume)
Domain_Adjustment = 1.00
Platform_Fee% = 8.5% × 0.90 × 1.00 × 0.95 × 1.00 = 7.27%
Platform_Fee = $10,000 × 7.27% = $727
Minimum check: $727 > $100 minimum → Valid

8.3 Fee Allocation

graph LR
subgraph "Fee Payment Options"
A[Option 1:<br/>Consumer Pays All]
B[Option 2:<br/>Split Proportionally]
C[Option 3:<br/>Initiator Pays]
D[Option 4:<br/>Absorbed in Distribution]
end
subgraph "Default by Model"
A --> |Fixed Price| F1[Default: Option 1<br/>Consumer pays all fees]
B --> |Revenue Share| F2[Default: Option 2<br/>Deducted from revenue]
D --> |Cost-Plus| F3[Default: Option 4<br/>Included in cost stack]
A --> |Barter| F4[Default: Option 1<br/>Initiator pays cash fee]
B --> |Hybrid| F5[Negotiable per component]
end
style A fill:#e1f5fe
style B fill:#e8f5e9
style C fill:#fff3e0

8. Trust & Reputation System
8.1 Trust Score Computation

8.1.1 Score Components & Weights

Trust_Score = Σ (Component_i × Weight_i) for i = 1 to 8
Score range: 0-100
Tiers: Bronze (0-39), Silver (40-59), Gold (60-74), Platinum (75-100)

8.1.2 Component Formulas
1. Transaction History (W_tx = 0.25)
TX_Score = min(100, Base_TX + Volume_Bonus + Value_Bonus + Consistency_Bonus)
Base_TX = min(50, Completed_Deals × 10) # 5 deals = 50 points
Volume_Bonus = min(20, (Completed_Deals - 5) × 2) # +2 per deal after 5
Value_Bonus = min(15, Total_Value / $100,000 × 15) # Max at $100K total
Consistency_Bonus = min(15, Monthly_Avg × 3) # Regular activity bonus
Penalty:
- Deal cancellation (after acceptance): -5 per cancellation
- No-Show (accepted but didn't participate): -10 per incident
- Deal timeout (no response): -2 per timeout

2. Review Ratings (W_rev = 0.20)
REV_Score = Weighted_Avg_Rating × 20 # Convert 1-5 scale to 0-100
Weighted_Avg_Rating = Σ (Rating_j × Reviewer_Trust_j) / Σ Reviewer_Trust_j
Where:
Rating_j = average of multi-dimensional ratings for review j
Reviewer_Trust_j = trust score of the party who left the review (normalized 0-1)
Multi-dimensional ratings (each 1-5):
- Communication: Was responsive and clear
- Reliability: Delivered as promised
- Value Delivered: Met or exceeded expectations
- Fairness: Acted fairly in negotiations and execution
Review Score = (Communication + Reliability + Value + Fairness) / 4
Minimum Reviews: Score starts at 50 (neutral) until 3 reviews received

3. Profile Completeness (W_prof = 0.10)
PROF_Score = sum of completed sections:
Basic info (name, photo): 20 points
Bio/Description:
15 points
Location verified:
10 points
Business details:
15 points

Portfolio/Past work:
15 points
Skills/Specializations:
10 points
Availability/Preferences: 10 points
External links:
5 points
─────────────────────────────
Maximum:
100 points

4. Verification Level (W_ver = 0.15)
VER_Score = sum of verification levels:
Email verified:
10 points
Phone verified:
15 points
Government ID verified:
30 points
Business registration:
25 points
Bank account linked:
10 points
Professional certification: 10 points
─────────────────────────────
Maximum:
100 points (or 110 with bonus)
Bonus: +10 for video verification interview

5. Response Rate (W_resp = 0.10)
RESP_Score = Response_Rate × 80 + Timeliness_Score × 20
Response_Rate = Responses_Sent / Messages_Received (last 90 days)
Capped at 1.0 (100%)
Timeliness_Score = based on average response time:
< 1 hour: 100 points
< 4 hours: 80 points
< 24 hours: 60 points
< 48 hours: 40 points
< 72 hours: 20 points
> 72 hours: 0 points

6. Dispute History (W_disp = 0.10)
DISP_Score = 100 - Dispute_Penalty
Dispute_Penalty = Disputes_Filed_Against × Severity_Factor +
Disputes_Lost × 15 +
Pattern_Penalty
Severity_Factor:
Resolved amicably: 5 points
Mediated resolution: 10 points
Lost arbitration: 20 points
Pattern_Penalty:
3+ disputes in 6 months: additional 10 points
5+ disputes in 6 months: additional 25 points
Floor: 0 points (can't go negative)

7. Platform Longevity (W_age = 0.05)
AGE_Score = min(100, Account_Age_Days / 10)
# 1000 days (~2.7 years) = maximum score
Decay: -1 point per 30 days of inactivity after 90 days

8. Community Contribution (W_comm = 0.05)
COMM_Score = min(100,
Successful_Referrals × 10 +
Helpful_Answers × 5 +
Mentor_Sessions × 15 +
Community_Recognition × 20
)

8.1.3 Final Trust Score Formula

TRUST_SCORE = (0.25 × TX_Score +
0.20 × REV_Score +
0.10 × PROF_Score +
0.15 × VER_Score +
0.10 × RESP_Score +
0.10 × DISP_Score +
0.05 × AGE_Score +
0.05 × COMM_Score)
Bounds: 0 <= TRUST_SCORE <= 100
Tier Assignment:
Platinum: 75-100
Gold: 60-74
Silver: 40-59
Bronze: 0-39
Decay: If no activity for 180 days, score decays by 2 points/month

8.3 Review Mechanism

8.3.1 Review Rules

ELIGIBILITY:
- Only parties who completed a deal together can review
- Review window: 7 days after deal completion
- Extension: Up to 14 days if dispute filed
- Minimum interaction: Deal must have progressed past escrow release
ANONYMITY:
- Reviews are attributed (party name visible)
- Individual dimension ratings are anonymous
- Written feedback is attributed
VISIBILITY:
- Reviews revealed simultaneously to ALL parties
- Timing: 72 hours after first review submitted OR
7 days after deal completion (whichever is later)
- Prevents retaliatory reviews

EDITING:
- Reviews can be edited within 48 hours of submission
- After reveal: reviews are permanent
- Follow-up reviews allowed for ongoing deals (monthly)

8.3.2 Review Challenge Process

graph TD
A[Review Published] --> B{Party disputes<br/>review?}
B -->|No| C[Review remains public]
B -->|Yes| D[Submit challenge<br/>with evidence]
D --> E[Platform moderates<br/>within 48 hours]
E --> F{Challenge valid?}
F -->|Yes| G[Options for challenger:]
G --> H1[Remove review]
G --> H2[Edit review text]
G --> H3[Add response note]
F -->|No| I[Review stands]
I --> J[Challenger gets<br/>strike on record]
J --> K{3 strikes?}
K -->|Yes| L[Review privilege<br/>suspended 30 days]
K -->|No| C
H1 --> C
H2 --> C
H3 --> C

8.3.3 Review Weighting

Effective_Rating = Raw_Rating × Reviewer_Weight × Recency_Weight ×
Deal_Value_Weight
Reviewer_Weight = Reviewer_Trust_Score / 100
# Reviews from highly-trusted parties count more
Recency_Weight:
Last 90 days: 1.0
91-180 days: 0.85
181-365 days: 0.70
1-2 years:
0.50
> 2 years:
0.30
Deal_Value_Weight = min(1.5, sqrt(Deal_Value / $10,000))
# Larger deals have more weight, capped at 1.5x

8. Risk Management
8.1 Escrow Design

8.1.1 Escrow Architecture

graph TD
subgraph "Escrow Flow"
C[Consumer] -->|Deposit 100%| E[Escrow Account]
E -->|Hold| H[Held Funds]
H -->|Milestone 1| S1[Supplier: 30%]
H -->|Milestone 1| E1[Enhancer: 20%]
H -->|Platform fee| P1[Platform: 10%]
H -->|Milestone 2| S2[Supplier: 20%]
H -->|Milestone 2| E2[Enhancer: 15%]
H -->|Final delivery| S3[Supplier: Final]
H -->|Final delivery| E3[Enhancer: Final]
end

subgraph "Escrow Release Conditions"
RC1[Condition Types]
RC1 --> RC2[Party consensus
All 3 agree]
RC1 --> RC3[Oracle verification
External data]
RC1 --> RC4[Milestone deadline
Auto if no dispute]
RC1 --> RC5[Third-party inspection
Professional verifier]
end

8.1.2 Escrow Amount & Holdback

Escrow_Deposit = Deal_Value × Escrow_Percentage
Escrow_Percentage by Trust Score:
Platinum (90+): 25% (75% released on proof of work)
Gold (75-89):
50% (50% released on proof of work)
Silver (60-74): 75% (25% released on proof of work)
Bronze (40-59): 100% (full escrow required)
Below 40:
100% + 20% Collateral
Holdback_Reserve = Deal_Value × 5% (held until final confirmation)
Release Triggers:
1. Party Consensus: All 3 parties confirm → immediate release
2. Timeout: If no dispute filed within dispute_window (7 days) → auto-release
3. Oracle: External verification condition met → auto-release
4. Mediator: Approved mediator signs off → release
Partial Release (milestone deals):
At each milestone M: Release_P(M) = Total_Payout_P × Milestone_Weight_M

8.2.1 Insurance Options
Deal Insurance Tiers:

Basic ($0.50 per $100 deal value):
- Covers: Non-delivery by counterparty
- Payout: Up to 50% of escrow
- Deductible: $500
Standard ($1.00 per $100 deal value):
- Covers: Non-delivery, quality defects, fraud
- Payout: Up to 100% of escrow
- Deductible: $250
- Includes: Mediation cost coverage
Premium ($2.50 per $100 deal value):
- Covers: All of above + force majeure, market loss, currency risk
- Payout: Up to 150% of deal value
- Deductible: $0
- Includes: Full dispute resolution, legal support
Platform Fund: 2% of all fees allocated to a mutual insurance pool
for cases where individual insurance doesn't apply.

8.2.2 Collateral Requirements

Collateral_Required = max(0, Risk_Score × Deal_Value - Escrow_Coverage)
Risk_Score = f(Party_Trust, Deal_Size, Domain_Risk, Counterparty_Trust)
Trust < 40: Risk_Score = 0.30
Trust 40-59: Risk_Score = 0.15
Trust 60-74: Risk_Score = 0.08
Trust 75+: Risk_Score = 0.03
Deal > $100K: +0.05
Deal > $500K: +0.10
New domain: +0.05
Collateral Form:
- Cash deposit (preferred)
- Bank guarantee/letter of credit
- Cryptocurrency (with 150% value requirement for volatility)
- Asset-backed security (platform-approved assets)

Collateral Return:
- Full return: Upon successful deal completion
- Partial return: If dispute resolved in party's favor
- Forfeiture: If party found at fault in dispute

8.3 Fraud Prevention

graph TD
subgraph "Fraud Detection Pipeline"
A[New Account/Deal] --> B{Automated Screening}
B --> C[Identity Verification]
C --> C1[Document OCR + forgery check]
C --> C2[Biometric liveness check]
C --> C3[Database cross-reference]
B --> D[Behavioral Analysis]
D --> D1[Typing pattern analysis]
D --> D2[Device fingerprinting]
D --> D3[IP/geolocation check]
B --> E[Deal Pattern Detection]
E --> E1[Price anomaly detection]
E --> E2[Circular deal detection]
E --> E3[Velocity checks]
C1 & C2 & C3 --> F{Risk Score > Threshold?}
D1 & D2 & D3 --> F
E1 & E2 & E3 --> F
F -->|Yes| G[Enhanced Review]
G --> G1[Manual verification]
G --> G2[Delay deal 48 hours]
G --> G3[Require additional collateral]
F -->|No| H[Clear for platform]
G1 --> I{Confirmed fraud?}
I -->|Yes| J[Account banned
Funds frozen
Law enforcement notified]
I -->|No| H
end

Fraud Detection Rules:
AUTO-FLAG TRIGGERS:
1. New account + deal > $50K within 48 hours → Enhanced review
2. Price 50%+ below market benchmark → Manual review
3. Same device/IP creating multiple accounts → Block + investigate
4. Circular deal pattern (A→B→C→A) → Block all parties
5. Payment from high-risk jurisdiction → Enhanced KYC
6. Rapid-fire deal proposals (>10/day) → Rate limit + review

7. Reviews from same IP/network → Review weight = 0
8. Profile photo reverse-image search fail → Require re-verification
9. Bank account name mismatch → Block until resolved
10. Chargeback history >5% → Account restricted
RISK SCORING:
Each trigger adds points to a risk score (0-100)
0-30: Green - Normal processing
31-60: Yellow - Enhanced monitoring
61-80: Orange - Manual review required
81-100: Red - Block until cleared

8.4 Dispute Resolution

8.4.1 Three-Tier Resolution System

graph TD
A[Dispute Filed] --> B{Tier 1:<br/>Direct Negotiation}
B -->|Resolved in 7 days| C[Agreement documented<br/>Escrow released per terms]
B -->|Not resolved| D{Tier 2:<br/>Platform Mediation}
D --> E[Mediator assigned<br/>within 24 hours]
E --> F[Evidence collection<br/>5-day window]
F --> G[Mediator proposal<br/>within 3 days]
G -->|All parties accept| C
G -->|Rejected| H{Tier 3:<br/>Binding Arbitration}
H --> I[Arbitrator panel<br/>3 industry experts]
I --> J[Formal hearing<br/>within 14 days]
J --> K[Binding decision<br/>within 7 days]
K --> L[Decision enforced<br/>Escrow distributed]
K --> M[Loser pays<br/>arbitration costs]
C --> N[Dispute logged
Party scores updated]
L --> N
M --> N

8.4.2 Dispute Process Details
Tier 1: Direct Negotiation (Days 1-7)
Initiation: Any party files dispute with description and claim
Process:
- 48-hour cooling-off period
- Structured negotiation chat with templates
- Platform suggests fair splits based on deal terms
- Automatic extension available (once, +7 days)
Cost: Free
Success Rate Target: 65%

Tier 2: Platform Mediation (Days 8-18)

Initiation: Auto-escalated if Tier 1 fails
Mediator: Platform-trained mediator (industry expert)
Process:
- Mediator reviews all evidence
- Separate confidential sessions with each party
- Mediator proposes settlement (non-binding)
- If accepted: documented and executed
- If rejected: escalates to Tier 3
Evidence Accepted:
- Chat logs (automatically captured)
- Delivery confirmations
- Third-party inspection reports
- Photos/videos with timestamps
- Financial transaction records
Cost: $200 (split equally, refunded if settlement reached)
Success Rate Target: 25% (of remaining disputes)

Tier 3: Binding Arbitration (Days 19-45)
Panel: 3 arbitrators (1 chosen by each party, 1 platform-appointed)
Process:
- Formal evidence submission (10-day window)
- Virtual hearing (each party presents case)
- Deliberation and binding decision
- Decision enforced by platform (escrow distributed)
Cost: $1,500 + 2% of disputed amount
Loser pays all costs (split 50/50 if mixed decision)
Decision Types:
- Full refund to one party
- Proportional split
- Partial refund with damages
- Rework/replacement order
- Deal cancellation with penalty assignment
Success Rate Target: 100% (binding)

8.4.3 Penalty Structure

DISPUTE OUTCOME PENALTIES:
For party found at fault:
- Trust Score: -15 to -30 points (based on severity)
- Escrow forfeiture: 10-50% of held amount
- Platform fee premium: +10% for next 3 deals
- Review flag: "Dispute: Found at fault" on profile
Severity levels:
Minor (communication, minor delay): -15 points, 10% escrow
Moderate (quality issue, partial non-delivery): -20 points, 25% escrow
Major (fraud, complete non-delivery): -30 points, 50% escrow, account review

For party filing frivolous dispute:
- Trust Score: -10 points
- Forfeit dispute fee
- Warning on profile
- 3 frivolous disputes = suspension
For mutual fault:
- Both parties: -10 points
- Escrow split 50/50
- No additional penalties

8.5 Market Risk Management

Price Volatility Protection:
1. Price Lock: Fixed price deals lock at proposal acceptance
2. Price Band: Revenue share deals can specify min/max price
3. Indexed Pricing: Prices tied to commodity index (e.g., wheat futures)
4. Collar: Price floor and ceiling defined upfront
Force Majeure:
1. Deal automatically suspended
2. No penalties for non-delivery during force majeure
3. Insurance claims triggered
4. Renegotiation window opens after force majeure ends
5. If renegotiation fails within 30 days: deal cancelled, escrow returned pro-rata
Domain-Specific Risk Adjustments:
Agriculture: Weather insurance, crop yield guarantees
Manufacturing: Quality inspection bonds, delivery insurance
Technology: IP escrow, code escrow for SaaS deals
Real Estate: Title insurance, appraisal requirements

Multi-Party Risk Check:
Total_Exposure_P = Σ Active_Deal_Values for party P
If Total_Exposure_P > Max_Outstanding:
→ Block new deals until exposure reduced
→ Suggest completing or insuring current deals

8.3 Market Maker Role

Platform as Market Maker:

When a domain has insufficient supply:
1. Platform becomes temporary Supplier or Enhancer
2. Platform sources resources at wholesale, provides at retail
3. Platform takes margin risk to ensure Consumer demand is met
4. Gradually replaces platform supply with third-party supply
Example: Farm land domain
- Platform leases 500 acres directly from landowners
- Platform offers these to Consumers with Enhancer matching
- As independent Suppliers join, platform reduces its inventory
- Target: Platform <10% of supply within 12 months per domain
Economic Impact:
- Reduces chicken-egg problem
- Ensures Consumer experience (always supply available)
- Generates early revenue (platform keeps full margin)
- Provides market data for pricing benchmarks

8.4 Subsidization Strategy

Optimal Subsidization: Subsidize the HARDER side to acquire
Framework:
If Suppliers > Enhancers > Consumers (in signup ease):
→ Subsidize Consumers (fee discounts, first-deal guarantee)
→ Subsidize Enhancers (service credits, visibility boost)
If Consumers > Suppliers > Enhancers:
→ Subsidize Enhancers (input cost coverage, guaranteed payment)
→ Subsidize Suppliers (land value guarantee, no-risk trial)
Dynamic Subsidy Allocation:
Subsidy_Budget_per_Domain = $10,000/month initially
Allocate based on supply/demand ratio:
If Supplier/Consumer ratio < 0.5: 50% to supplier acquisition
If Supplier/Consumer ratio > 2.0: 50% to consumer acquisition
Otherwise: Balanced across all parties
Subsidy Forms (in order of preference):
1. Fee credits (low cash cost, high perceived value)
2. Escrow guarantees (builds trust, contingent cost)
3. Direct payment (only for anchor partners)
4. Revenue share (performance-linked)

8.6 Domain Expansion Economics
Domain Expansion Framework:

Phase 1: Market Research (2 weeks, $5,000)
- TAM analysis
- Party density assessment
- Competitive landscape
- Regulatory requirements
Phase 2: Soft Launch (4 weeks, $15,000)
- Recruit 20 anchor parties per role
- Seed 5-10 initial deals
- Calibrate pricing benchmarks
- Validate unit economics
Phase 3: Full Launch (8 weeks, $30,000)
- Marketing campaign
- Full feature enablement
- Community building
- PR and case studies
Go/No-Go Criteria:
GO if: 20+ parties per role signed, 5+ deals completed,
positive NPS from pilot users
NO-GO if: <10 parties per role after 4 weeks,
no deals completed, regulatory barriers
Domain Priority Matrix:
Score = TAM × Accessibility × Strategic_Fit × Platform_Synergy
Priority 1 (Score >70): Launch immediately
Priority 2 (Score 50-70): Launch within 6 months
Priority 3 (Score 30-49): Evaluate further
Priority 4 (Score <30): Do not pursue

Price indices]
O --> OR5[IoT Sensors
Real-time monitoring]
end

8.2 Milestone-Triggered Automatic Payments
// Pseudocode: Milestone Payment Contract
contract ThreePartyDeal {
struct Milestone {
bytes32 id;
string description;
uint256 paymentAmount;
address paymentTo;
// Supplier, Enhancer, or split
TriggerType triggerType;
bytes32 triggerCondition;
bool verified;
uint256 deadline;
uint256 completedAt;
}
enum TriggerType {

}

TIME_BASED,
// e.g., "30 days after planting"
ORACLE_FEED,
// e.g., "rainfall > 50mm"
PARTY_CONSENSUS, // All 3 parties confirm
THIRD_PARTY_VERIFY, // Inspector signs off
EXTERNAL_EVENT
// API callback (delivery confirmed)

// Milestone completion triggers automatic payment
function completeMilestone(bytes32 milestoneId, bytes proof) external {
Milestone storage m = milestones[milestoneId];
require(!m.verified, "Already verified");
require(isTriggerMet(m.triggerType, m.triggerCondition, proof),
"Trigger condition not met");
m.verified = true;
m.completedAt = block.timestamp;
// Auto-release payment from escrow
releaseEscrow(milestoneId, m.paymentTo, m.paymentAmount);
emit MilestoneCompleted(milestoneId, msg.sender, m.paymentAmount);

}

// Check if all milestones complete → release holdback
if (allMilestonesComplete()) {
releaseHoldback();
}

// Oracle callback for external verification
function oracleCallback(bytes32 milestoneId, bool conditionMet, bytes signature)
external onlyAuthorizedOracle {

}

require(conditionMet, "Oracle reports condition not met");
completeMilestone(milestoneId, signature);

// Dispute timelock: If no dispute filed within window, auto-release
function checkTimelock(bytes32 milestoneId) external {
Milestone storage m = milestones[milestoneId];
require(m.verified, "Milestone not yet verified");
require(block.timestamp > m.completedAt + DISPUTE_WINDOW,
"Dispute window still open");
require(!m.disputed, "Dispute filed");

}

}

// Auto-release to designated party
finalizePayment(milestoneId);

8.3 Conditional Execution Logic

CONDITIONAL PAYMENT TYPES:
1. IF-THEN Payments:
IF [condition] THEN release [amount] to [party]
Example: IF crop_yield > 5_tons_per_acre
THEN release bonus $500 to Enhancer
2. GRADUATED Payments:
Payment varies based on continuous metric
Example: Quality_Score 1-10 → Payment = Base × (0.7 + 0.03 × Score)
Score 5 → 85% of base
Score 8 → 94% of base
Score 10 → 100% of base
3. PENALTY Payments:
Deduction for missed targets
Example: Delivery_delay_days × $100/day deduction from Supplier payment
Max penalty: 20% of total payment
4. BONUS Payments:
Extra reward for exceeding targets
Example: Revenue > $20,000 → 10% of excess as bonus to all parties
5. CONTINGENT Payments:
Payment only if future event occurs
Example: IF product wins industry award within 1 year
THEN $5,000 bonus to Enhancer from revenue share

Oracle Security:
- Multi-oracle consensus: Require 2 of 3 oracles to agree
- Staked oracles: Oracles post collateral, slashed if incorrect
- Decentralized oracle networks (Chainlink integration)
- Fallback to manual verification if oracle disagreement

8.5 Smart Contract Deployment Flow

graph TD

J --> K{Condition<br/>verified?}
K -->|Yes| L[Auto-release payment]
K -->|No| M[Hold payment<br/>flag for review]
I -->|No| N{Dispute<br/>filed?}
N -->|Yes| O[Pause auto-execution]

N -->|No| Q{All milestones<br/>complete?}
Q -->|No| H

R --> S[Deal CLOSED]
L --> H
M --> H
P --> H

Appendix A: Mathematical Formula Reference
A.1 Value Distribution Formulas

Fixed Price:
Platform_Fee = Deal_Value × Fee%
Net_Pool = Deal_Value - Platform_Fee
Supplier_Payout = Net_Pool × Supplier_Share%
Enhancer_Payout = Net_Pool × Enhancer_Share%
Revenue Share:
Distributable = Gross_Revenue × (1 - Platform_Fee% - Reserve%)
Party_Payout_P = Distributable × Share_P%
Cost-Plus:
Total_Cost = Supplier_Cost + Enhancer_Cost + Platform_Cost
Final_Price = Total_Cost × (1 + Margin_%)
Party_Payout_P = Cost_P × (1 + Margin_P%)
Hybrid:
Total = Upfront + Σ Milestone_i + Revenue_Share_Component
Each component uses respective formula

A.2 Trust Score Formula

TRUST_SCORE = Σ (Component_i × Weight_i)
Components:
TX_Score = min(100, Deals×10 + max(0,(Deals-5)×2) + Value/$100K×15 + Monthly×3)
REV_Score = 20 × Σ(Rating_j × ReviewerTrust_j) / Σ ReviewerTrust_j
PROF_Score = sum of profile section completions (max 100)
VER_Score = sum of verification levels (max 100 + 10 bonus)
RESP_Score = ResponseRate × 80 + Timeliness × 20
DISP_Score = 100 - (LostDisputes×15 + FiledAgainst×Severity + PatternPenalty)
AGE_Score = min(100, Days/10)
COMM_Score = min(100, Referrals×10 + Answers×5 + Mentor×15)
Weights: 0.25, 0.20, 0.10, 0.15, 0.10, 0.10, 0.05, 0.05

A.3 Dynamic Pricing Formula

Fee% = 8.5% × Trust_Mult × Complexity_Mult × Volume_Discount × Domain_Adj
Trust_Mult:
Platinum (90+): 0.80
Gold (75-89): 0.90
Silver (60-74): 1.00
Bronze (40-59): 1.15
<40:
1.35
Complexity_Mult: 0.90 / 1.00 / 1.25
Volume_Discount: 1.00 / 0.95 / 0.90 / 0.85
Domain_Adj: 0.95 to 1.20 depending on domain

A.4 Fairness Score

Fairness = 0.25×Abs_Gain + 0.30×Prop_Fair + 0.25×Benchmark + 0.20×Opp_Cost
Abs_Gain = min(1.0, max(0, min(Gain_P)) / (max(Gain_P) × 0.5))
Prop_Fair = max(0, 1 - variance(Shares) × 10)
Benchmark = avg(max(0, 1 - |premium_P| × 2))
Opp_Cost = avg(1.0 if net_benefit > 0 else max(0, 0.5 + net_benefit/OC))

Appendix B: Decision Tree Summary

graph TD
START[Platform Interaction] --> Q{New or<br/>Existing User?}
Q -->|New| ONBOARD[Onboarding Flow]
ONBOARD --> V1[Verify Identity<br/>Build Profile]
V1 --> T1[Initial Trust Score: 35]
T1 --> BROWSE[Browse Deals<br/>$10K limit]

9. Cross-Cutting Concerns
This section integrates security, observability, compliance, and audit considerations that span
across all architectural layers and domains described in Chapters 3 through 8. These concerns
are implemented as shared infrastructure services and policies applied consistently across all
microservices.

9.2.3 Distributed Tracing
All API requests include correlation headers (X-Request-ID, X-Correlation-ID, X-B3-TraceId,
X-B3-SpanId) that propagate through the service mesh. Traces capture: - Request latency per
service hop - Database query execution times - External API call latencies - Event
publishing/consuming timestamps

distributing escrowed funds according to the value
distribution model.
A party offering resources or assets that can be leveraged by
other parties.
A specific condition or parameter of a deal being negotiated
(e.g., price, timeline, deliverables).

Definition
A category of terms being negotiated (e.g., Value
Distribution, Deliverables, Timeline, Roles &
Responsibilities, Risk & Termination).
A composite reputation metric (0-100) derived from
reviews, completion history, and platform behavior. See
Chapter 8, Section 8.4.
The allocation of monetary or non-monetary value among
the three parties in a deal.
An immutable object without identity, defined solely by its
attributes (e.g., GeoPoint, Money).
A deal sub-state where deliverables are inspected against
acceptance criteria before payment release.
The core platform principle that all three parties must derive
positive net value from a deal. See Chapter 8, Section 8.1.
Zone of Possible Agreement — the overlap between party
acceptable ranges for a given term dimension.

read models;

Alternatives Rejected

Consequences

Direct payment: high risk
of non-payment or nondelivery. Letter of credit:
too slow and expensive for
smaller deals. Blockchain
escrow: considered for
Phase 4 but adds
complexity for MVP.

Requires
payment
provider
integration;
escrow fees
increase
platform cost;
funds held
create
regulatory
considerations.

Single model: would
compromise both read and
write performance. Direct
DB reads: would couple
read clients to write
schema.

Eventual
consistency
between write
and read
models; need
for projection
infrastructure;
increased
system
complexity.

Alternatives Rejected

Consequences

RabbitMQ: excellent for
simple routing but less

NATS: lightweight but
fewer enterprise features.
Pulsar: promising but
smaller ecosystem.

Operational
complexity of
Kafka cluster;
need for careful
topic design and
monitoring.

REST for internal: higher
latency, no strong typing.
GraphQL for internal:
overkill for service-toservice. Message queue
only: insufficient for
request-response patterns.

Requires proto
definitions and
code
generation; less
human-readable
for debugging;
load balancer
considerations
for HTTP/2.

Alternatives Rejected

Consequences

MongoDB: eventual
consistency model
unsuitable for financial
transactions. MySQL:
fewer advanced features.
CockroachDB: interesting
for global distribution but
higher operational cost.

Single-writer
bottleneck per
aggregate;
requires careful
sharding
strategy for
scale.

Manual review: too slow,
subjective, doesn’t scale.
Simple percentage rules:
insufficient for complex
value types. No validation:
would lead to unfair deals
and platform
abandonment.

Computationall
y intensive;
requires
accurate market
data; may reject
borderline deals
that humans
would approve.

2PC (Two-Phase
Commit): too slow, creates
locks, not suitable for
microservices. TCC (TryConfirm-Cancel): more
efficient but complex to
implement.

Eventual
consistency;
need for
compensating
transaction
design; requires
idempotent
operations.

explain. Binary

Version: 1.0
Date: June 2026
Status: Draft for Review
Classification: Confidential

This document integrates six specialist-authored design documents into a single unified
software design specification. All content has been preserved with consistent terminology,
renumbered sections, and added cross-references between chapters.
